1935.02.16

Regarding Construction and Pacification: Defining Central Tasks 1

Furthermore, Order Three Provinces to Strangle and Suppress Military Officers: Set a Deadline to Eliminate Remnant Bandits in Border Areas; Otherwise, They Will Be Deemed as Harboring Bandits and Disobeying Orders

[Nanchang] Chairman Chiang, on the 15th, telegraphed Zhang, Acting Commander of Hubei; Director He; Chairman Zhang of Hunan; Chairman Liu of Henan; Chairman Liu of Anhui; Director Gu of Jiangxi; Chairman Xiong; Director Chiang of Zhangzhou; and Chairman Chen of Fujian, stating that each province should henceforth define its central tasks for construction and pacification. The original telegram read: "Upon investigation, the five provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Fujian have long suffered from banditry. They have just been pacified, leaving the local areas devastated and full of wounds. The most urgent task in the aftermath is to strive for construction to achieve recovery, to implement thorough pacification to eliminate remnants, and especially to ensure military and political cooperation, with the army and civilians working together to quickly promote the practical effects of construction and pacification. Starting from March this year, the pacification commanders and administrative commissioners of each district should jointly select one or two construction projects and central tasks in pacification to focus on with utmost concentration and collective effort. Each period should be three months. Each period must be carried out in accordance with its predetermined plan. The central tasks for the first period must be completed by the end of May this year. The implementation methods of the selected tasks should be submitted through each pacification headquarters and provincial government to the General Headquarters for record. Provinces without a pacification district commander should have the local stationed army commander or division commander cooperate with the administrative commissioner of the district to handle matters in accordance with the above regulations. The stationed troops in the district should provide as much assistance as possible for this task. When this chairman arrives in the area for inspection, the effectiveness will be used as a basis for performance evaluation. The central tasks for the second period may continue unfinished projects from the first period or be stipulated separately, and must also be reported at the same time. It is hoped that the corresponding pacification zone commanders or unit officers and administrative commissioners will be instructed to strictly comply with these requirements." (Deleted by Zhongzheng, Central News Agency dispatch on the 15th)

[Nanchang] Chairman Chiang, on the 15th, telegraphed Zhang Xueliang and the general commanders and division commanders in the border areas of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, setting a deadline of April this year to eliminate the remnant bandits in the border areas; otherwise, they will be charged with harboring bandits and disobeying orders. The original telegram read: "Upon investigation, the remnant bandits in the border areas have been repeatedly attacked and their nests destroyed. They are already in dire straits and unable to do anything. However, the bandit suppression troops in the border areas, although having formed a long-standing encirclement, have not achieved complete annihilation. For two years, the bandit gangs have been able to survive and arbitrarily roam around. This is not because the remnant bandits are particularly cunning, but because our bandit suppression troops are slow to act and ineffective in pursuing and suppressing them. It is a waste of resources and money, harmful to the local areas, and a failure to protect the country and its people. Speaking of this, I feel deeply saddened. From now on, the Liang General Commander, the Liu Army Commander, and the He Army Commander should be separately responsible for supervising and intensifying the suppression efforts. Before April this year, all important bandit leaders in the border areas must be captured or killed. Otherwise, the general commanders, army commanders, and officers of the subordinate units will be held responsible and charged with harboring bandits and disobeying orders. All should comply strictly and not be negligent again." (Deleted by Zhongzheng, Central News Agency dispatch on the 15th)

Jiangxi Provincial Cooperation Association Presents a Large Banner to Chairman Chiang 2

Also, a Large Silver Cauldron and Congratulatory Words

[Nanchang] The Provincial Cooperation Association, to honor merit and repay virtue, specially prepared commemorative gifts to respectfully present to Chairman Chiang: a red satin banner, a large silver cauldron, and a congratulatory scroll. All the committee members presented them to Chairman Chiang. The congratulatory words read: "The Red Bandits' calamity in Jiangxi shook the world. Chairman, you were enraged and expeditiously marched, saving the people from fire and water, cutting through thorns and brambles, annihilating the great bandits, and recovering famous cities. The city dust is settled, and your authority and virtue are manifest. Jackals and wolves flee far away, and farming and weaving bring tranquility. As the Book of Changes says, 'Offerings bring blessings, and benevolence spreads with meritorious inscriptions.' Celebrating the triumphant return, we respectfully express our sincere heart." (Central News Agency dispatch on the 15th)

The Japanese-Puppet Side Expedites Construction of Two Roads Outside the Pass 3

[Tianjin] The puppet regime allocated 1,200,000 yuan to build the roads from Chengde to Shanhaiguan and from Chengde to Gubeikou. Construction has not started because enough workers have not been recruited. Both roads are entrusted to the South Manchuria Railway Company by the puppet Ministry of Transportation to build. The routes connecting Chengde to Gubeikou, Chengde to Xifengkou, and Chengde to Lengkou are each constructing a highway about two zhang wide for automobile traffic. The surveying has been completed. The puppet government stipulates discounts for the price of the occupied land for each road. When the two roads are completed, they will connect with the Jinzhou-Chaoyang Road, making military transportation more convenient. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

[Tianjin] The Shandaitong Company in Shanhaiguan specializes in selling puppet entry permits. Recently, entrusted by the Japanese and puppet authorities, it is recruiting laborers in the pass and transporting them outside the pass to build roads. The company has branches in Dalian, Yingkou, Changchun, Shenyang, Gubeikou, and Xifengkou, and has a four-part organization with free lodging, job placement, career guidance, and disease relief. The recruited laborers are all recruited by the company. However, although there are such organizations, they are actually false to strengthen people's trust. Once they enter the puppet territory, all organizations become surveillance agencies, forcing work and not paying a penny. The authorities of Hebei have issued a circular to all subordinates, dissuading laborers from being deceived. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

[Dalian] The Chinese steamer Xinhua, carrying 230 Chinese coolies, was refused entry because they did not have entry permits. Among them, 158 people actually boarded five sampans and landed privately today. After being discovered on the spot, orders have been issued to search strictly. (Reuters dispatch on the 15th)

Huludao Project Actively Underway by the Japanese Side 4

[Tianjin] The Huludao project has completed the first, second, and third phases of construction. The Japanese side has scheduled the fourth phase of construction to begin in April, first building wharves number seven and eight, the Japanese naval headquarters, and the Japanese naval barracks, adding railway tracks, and building the dock for the warship Leixingzhuang in north Huludao. The fifth and sixth phases of construction will be carried out around July and August, focusing on tidying up municipal affairs. Currently, three Japanese warships are docked in the port to protect the ships. Japanese ships enter the port daily to load and unload goods. The amount of goods imported and exported through the puppet Fengshan Road is extremely large. There are already 300 shops, a population of over 40,000, and the industry is becoming increasingly prosperous. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

Yi Wo Visits Yu Xuezhong to Discuss War Zone Issues 5

New Peace Preservation Corps Enters War Zone: Number of Personnel and Equipment Largely Determined

Two District Commanders Have Been Appointed: Zhang Yantian and Zhang Qingyu

[Beiping] Yi Wo, accompanied by Tao Shangming, visited Yu Xuezhong at 9:00 AM this morning to discuss issues related to the war zone. Regarding the entry of the newly formed Peace Preservation Corps into the war zone, it was decided to maintain the quota of 5,000 personnel. In addition to carrying rifles, they will be allowed to carry 50 light machine guns to suppress banditry. Yi Wo stated that the number of light machine guns carried by the new Peace Preservation Corps should be inspected by the Japanese side at any time. Yu replied that constant inspection seemed too trivial and that it would be simpler to inspect when the new Peace Preservation Corps entered the war zone. The Japanese side has agreed. It is also heard that Yi Wo was very cheerful during the meeting. Yi Wo stated that if the Peace Preservation Corps needed artillery to suppress bandits, they could contact the Japanese side at any time to transport it for use, but it must be returned immediately after use. Yu also expressed satisfaction. The conversation ended at 10:30 AM. Yu told reporters that the date of entry of the new Peace Preservation Corps into the war zone has not been decided yet. The quota is 5,000 personnel, and the deployment of garrison locations will be based on the needs of the situation. Areas where the situation is stable may not need to be stationed. Areas where banditry has not subsided will naturally have a larger garrison. The two district commanders have been appointed as Zhang Yantian and Zhang Qingyu. Zhang Yantian will be stationed in the Luan-Yu district, and Zhang Qingyu will be stationed in the Ji-Mi district. As for the original Peace Preservation Corps, those with better discipline will be transferred to Tongxian. Feng Shoupeng's troops will be transferred to Kaiping and handed over to Zhao Lei for reorganization. Yi Wo left Beiping for Tianjin this afternoon. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

[Beiping] Since the resolution of the Chahar issue, the Japanese attitude towards North China diplomacy has gradually become more moderate than before. North China diplomacy is aimed at the central diplomatic policy, so it can be asserted that relations between the two sides will improve in the near future. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

[Beiping] Yu Xuezhong stated that the Yellow River breach blocking project in southern Hebei is being supervised on-site by Hu Yuanhui. The initial allocation of 200,000 yuan for the breach blocking project has been used up, and another 60,000 yuan has been allocated by the provincial government for use. The provincial government's move to Baoding will begin preparations next month. There are still insufficient houses for the government offices. The General Headquarters has agreed to find a way to vacate a part of the building. Banditry in Hebei Province has been quite successful after being suppressed by the stationed troops in various places. It is expected that it can be completely eliminated within this year. Regarding the sealing of Ji Hongchang's and Ren Yingqi's properties, the Hebei provincial government has not yet received instructions. To his personal knowledge, Ji and Ren have no property in Tianjin. He himself will not stay in Beiping for long and will report the recent military and political situation in Hebei Province to He this afternoon and return to Tianjin within days. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

[Tianjin] After the reorganization of the Yutian Peace Preservation Corps, it is planned to transfer them to Haiyangzhen, Kaiping, and Qinhuangdao. It will be implemented when the Qingwei meeting resolves the measures. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

[Tianjin] The Special Police Corps of Hebei will move east and be realized at the beginning of next month. The newly formed Special Police Corps of Zhang Yantian and Zhang Qingyu, stationed in Cangzhou, Jinghai, and Yangcun, will each be reduced to 2,500 personnel and renamed the Peace Preservation Corps. After moving east, the old Peace Preservation Corps of Fan Jinghe, Zhou Yuying, and Yang Yucheng will be replaced. They are allowed to carry 50 light machine guns. If necessary, with the consent of the Japanese side, heavy weapons can also be used. The maximum caliber of the field guns is 3.5. The Peace Preservation Corps of Zhao Lei and Liu Zuo Zhou will each be reduced to 1,500 personnel, and Sun Jizhou's troops will be reduced to 1,000 personnel, all called the Special Police Corps. The two types of Peace Preservation Corps and Special Police Corps have a total of 9,000 personnel, which conforms to the number agreed in the Tanggu Agreement. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

[Tianjin] Yi Wo came to Tianjin from Beiping this afternoon and plans to return to Yuguan by night train. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

[Tianjin] Feng Shoupeng's troops of the Yutian Peace Preservation Corps fought fiercely with more than 100 members of the Red Spear Society in Beisongzhuang for 8 hours, from 3:00 AM to 11:00 AM on the 13th. The Society members were unable to hold out and abandoned 32 corpses and fled into Yunshan Mountain. All the villages in the seventh district were looted by the Society members. The Red Spear Society members who infiltrated the seventh and eighth districts of Yutian County came from outside the pass. Initially, there were only 30 to 40 people. Later, they incited the ignorant people in Miaofeng Temple and expanded to more than 100 people. The Society's senior brother, Li, and second senior brother, Zhang, are both from Rehe. On the 12th, they once occupied Beisongzhuang and abducted 27 wealthy households such as Li Jiulong, and seized dozens of guns from the local defense forces and police stations. The bandits now have sharp weapons, so they are resisting stubbornly. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

[Beiping] The counties in the eastern and northern war zones of Hebei have been peaceful for the past month. Yutian only had a conflict in Linnancang two months ago, and it has been peaceful for the past two months. He Xiaoyi, the magistrate of Zunhua County, came to Beiping yesterday to meet with Yin Rugeng and report on everything, and he will return to his post in three or four days. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

[Beiping] After repeated consultations between China and Japan, the issue of the new Peace Preservation Corps entering the war zone has been largely decided. The number of personnel is 5,000. In addition to one gun per person, they will also carry 50 light machine guns. The Japanese side has also agreed that if they encounter a large number of bandits, they can temporarily add artillery and guns to suppress them, but they must be withdrawn afterwards. Preparations are currently underway, and they will enter the war zone after everything is ready. The new Peace Preservation Corps is divided into two brigades, led by Zhang Yantian and Zhang Qingyu. Zhang Yantian's troops will be stationed in the Luan-Yu district, and Zhang Qingyu's troops will be stationed in the Ji-Mi district. The details of the defense of the mines still need to be discussed. The original Peace Preservation Corps stationed in the war zone will select the better ones and transfer them to Tongzhou. The rest, such as Feng Shoupeng's troops, will be transferred to Kaiping for separate training. Whether to appoint a general commander or be commanded by the commissioner will be decided after entering the war zone, depending on the actual needs. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 15th)

Executive Yuan Orders All Provinces and Cities to Protect Sound Public Opinion 6

[Nanjing] The Executive Yuan ordered all provinces and cities that they should protect sound speech on one hand, and must not abuse their powers. The matters of censorship and prohibition should be strictly followed by laws and regulations, and not overstep. On the other hand, they should also earnestly inform local speech organizations, so that they can restrain themselves, encourage adherence to journalistic ethics, and not abuse the power of newspapers to harm the interests of the country and others, so that the national news industry can enter the right track, enhance the effectiveness of public opinion, and establish the foundation of the rule of law. All depend on this. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

Legislative Yuan Passes the Army, Navy, and Air Force Disciplinary Regulations 7

Passes the Draft Law on the Organization of the Maritime Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications; Amends Two Articles of the Organization Law of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau; Rejects the Explanation of Legal Cases by the Judicial Yuan

[Nanjing] The Legislative Yuan convened a meeting at 9:00 AM on the 15th, with 74 members present, including Lian Shenghai and Zhao Maohua. Sun Ke presided over the meeting, and Liang Han Cao was the secretary-general. The matters discussed were as follows: (1) Review and revise the articles of the Organization Law of the Salt Administration Reform Committee, decided to submit to the Legal System and Finance Committees for review. (2) Review and revise Articles 17, 20, 21, and 22 of the Organization Law of the Ministry of Education, decided to submit to the Legal System Committee for review. (3) The Military and Legal System Committees reported on the review of the draft Disciplinary Regulations for the Army, Navy, and Air Force, decided to revise and pass. (4) The Legal System Committee reported on the review of the draft Organization Law of the Maritime Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, decided to revise and pass. (5) The Legal System and Economic Committees reported on the review of the revision of Articles 4 and 6 of the Organization Law of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau, decided to pass according to the review report. According to the review results, Article 4 was changed to the bureau will have six divisions: General Affairs, Business, Accounting, Savings, Remittances, and Insurance. Each division will have a director and deputy director, selected by the director of the bureau from specialized personnel and submitted for appointment. Article 6 was changed to the bureau will have 60 to 100 staff members, submitted by the director of the bureau for appointment from specialized personnel who have passed the screening examination. As for the Legal System and Economic Committees' proposal to the Yuan Conference that all requests to the Yuan for the interpretation of legal cases should be interpreted by the Judicial Yuan according to law, after fierce debate among the members, it was finally rejected. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 15th)

[Nanjing] The Legislative Yuan passed the amended Army, Navy, and Air Force Disciplinary Law at the General Assembly on the 15th. All 24 articles stipulate that the misconduct of personnel of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, and military dependents, which does not involve the scope of criminal law, shall be punished according to this law, unless otherwise stipulated by law. The types of punishment for officers and warrant officers are removal from office, suspension, demerit, salary deduction, confinement, and sincere repentance; for soldiers, they are demotion, confinement, labor service, house arrest, reprimand. There are 26 items of punishable misconduct, including undermining military discipline, losing military reputation, forming private groups, shirking responsibility and claiming credit, using excuses to coerce, overstepping authority, and improper handling. The powers of punishment exercised by leaders at all levels over their subordinates are specified in detail. However, the punishment of officers and warrant officers above the rank of major general shall be submitted to the highest military authority for approval. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 15th)

[Nanjing] When the Legislative Yuan discussed the legal cases proposed by the Legal System and Economic Committees in the morning of the 15th, which should be interpreted by the Judicial Yuan, Jiao Yitang first explained the process of the proposal. The case was submitted by the Ministry of Industry to the Executive Yuan in 1931 and forwarded to the Legislative Yuan for interpretation. Article 10, Section 9, of the Ministry's Organization Law, whether the so-called special business includes savings associations. The Yuan Conference handed it over to the Legal System and Economic Committees for review. The two committees therefore raised the issue of the jurisdiction of legal interpretation, and the dispute was quite fierce. Some argued that according to Article 3 of the Judicial Yuan's Organization Law, the president of the Yuan, after deliberation by the president of the Supreme Court and the presidents of the subordinate courts, exercises the power to uniformly interpret laws and change precedents. The power of legal interpretation belongs to the judiciary, which is beyond doubt. If the Legislative Yuan also interprets laws, it not only hinders the uniformity of the power of interpretation, but also has the drawback of one law having two interpretations. Therefore, they supported the original proposal that the power of legal interpretation should belong to the judiciary. Some argued that the Legislative Yuan has interpreted laws in the first, second, and third sessions, which has become a convention. Moreover, the judicial interpretation of laws is limited to civil and criminal laws, and the interpretation of regulations on people's organizations and administrative regulations has always been done by the Legislative Yuan. The fourth session suddenly changed course, and the reasons were not appropriate. They opposed the original proposal and advocated waiting for the constitutional period before unifying the power of legal interpretation according to the provisions of the constitution. There were also proposals for compromise, advocating that judicial interpretation should still be handled by the Judicial Yuan, and legislative interpretation should be the responsibility of the Legislative Yuan. There were even those who advocated submitting the case for review. As a result, the chairman announced the vote. The case was rejected because the number of supporters was small, and it could not be established. As for the interpretation of the Organization Law of the Ministry of Industry, it was still handed over to the Legal System and Economic Committees for handling and reporting. The revised Organization Law of the Maritime Administration Bureau was also passed, and the Ministry of Communications also requested four amendments: (1) Regarding the handling of ship collision disputes, (2) Regarding the establishment of secretaries and inspectors. The legislators believed that the first point should be stipulated in the Maritime Dispute Handling Regulations, and the second point, the establishment of inspectors, may not be helpful. Moreover, not setting up secretaries has become a convention, and it does not seem necessary to amend it. (3) Regarding the qualifications for the appointment of maritime personnel, the Ministry of Communications' opinions were increased. (4) Regarding the establishment of offices, it was determined that they could be established in important seaports and commercial ports. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 15th)

Current Commentary

Another Method for Promoting the New Life Movement 8

— Heng

According to yesterday's newspaper report, Madam Chiang Kai-shek, Soong Mei-ling, donated a large sum of money to the Bible Society in this city, in accordance with President Chiang's promotion of the New Life Movement, so that it could reprint the Bible and spread it widely, in order to promote the practical effectiveness of the New Life Movement. The New Life Movement, since its inception by President Chiang, has been a year in the making. In this year, all parties have made sincere efforts to promote it, but in terms of effectiveness, it cannot but be said that it is still limited. China's national power has declined to the extreme today. Analyzing the reasons, the disloyalty of outsiders accounts for a small part, but the root causes of its own diseases account for the greater part. Zeng Guofan said, "The lack of soldiers is not enough to cry about, the lack of pay is not enough to worry deeply, only the inability to find someone who does not rush to seek profit before fulfilling righteousness is a cause for deep lament." This statement can be said to be on point. "People must insult themselves before others insult them. A country must attack itself before others attack it." If it does not first have its own way of decline and ruin, then what is there to fear even with foreign enemies? Therefore, if we want to save China from danger and ruin today, we can only start by curing the root causes of the disease. President Chiang promoted the New Life Movement and specifically revealed the four virtues of "propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame" as an advocacy for the people of the country. His motivation was not to be found in this. However, the reason why the results have not been great in the past year, despite the many efforts, is that the promotion of the New Life Movement in the past has purely started from the moral aspect. Morality is a major force governing life. This is something that no one can deny. However, morality is the fine words and deeds left to us by the ancient sages. Whether we can practice these fine words and deeds depends entirely on individual willpower. This is what makes it so difficult. Confucius once said, "At fifteen, I set my heart on learning; at thirty, I stood firm... At seventy, I could follow my heart's desire without transgressing the bounds of propriety." Even with the utmost holiness of Confucius, it still took fifty-five years of continuous effort to reach the point of "following my heart's desire without transgressing the bounds of propriety." It is thus evident how difficult it is for others to succeed. The moral precepts, whether practiced or not, are purely based on individual willingness. If one is unwilling, then the precepts are the precepts, and life is life. As for religion, it takes faith in a supernatural personality as a condition. Therefore, with faith, the moral precepts are not difficult to put into practice. As it is said, "as if He is above, as if He is on the left and right," even the common man and woman can do it. This is why the ancients had the saying of establishing teachings through divine ways. Now that Madam Chiang has seen this, it can truly open a new chapter for the New Life Movement.

Although Christianity has been in China for a long time, in the past, scholars and officials were less inclined to speak of it. In fact, the teachings of Christianity can be said to be a targeted medicine for today's widespread folk customs. There is a deep and urgent need for it. The Christian view of life is a non-individualistic and altruistic one. Because it does not take the individual as the center, it can encourage people to sacrifice themselves. Because it can sacrifice itself, it has the spirit of giving up one's life for righteousness. If the people of a country can mostly give up their lives for righteousness, I ask, would the country not become strong and prosperous as a result? Furthermore, the Christian view of life is both positive and negative. Because it is positive, it is a religion of this world. Because it is negative, it can encourage people not to strive for material things. To put it another way, the strength of Christianity lies in helping others. It always encourages people to provide positive assistance, but when they gain, it always advises people to yield. Therefore, its teachings neither deny material life nor affirm spiritual life at the same time. Because of this, it is clearly different from religions that escape the world. The greatest problems in our country today lie in the individualistic and materialistic views of life. Both of these lead people to selfishness and self-interest, from which they cannot recover. The reason why the nation has become a sheet of loose sand and the country's labor is becoming increasingly critical is that these two views of life are at work, and it is obvious that words of morality alone are not enough to save the day. Therefore, arousing people's religious beliefs to examine and restrain their bodies and minds is also a way to correct customs.

Moscow Newspaper Exposes Japan's Intentions in Coveting Chahar Province 9

Aimed at Striking Outer Mongolia to the North and Invading Our Northwest to the South; The Puppet State Sets Up a Mongolian Affairs Department and Includes Inner Mongolia Under Its Jurisdiction

[Moscow] The Pravda commented on the Chahar incident, "The Japanese warlords have long been paying attention to Chahar Province, Inner Mongolia, and the northwestern provinces of China. In Chahar, there are now a large number of highways, desert roads, and other roads leading directly to the Mongolian People's Republic. The Japanese warlords will use Chahar Province as a base for military operations, striking the Mongolian People's Republic to the north and invading the northwestern provinces of China to the south. At this time, we must point out that the 'Manchukuo' government has recently established the so-called Mongolian Affairs Department, and the vast area of Inner Mongolia has been included in the 'jurisdiction' of this department. At the same time, the department plans to annex northern Chahar into the 'Manchukuo' territory. The Chahar incident was caused by the mutiny of Japanese officers. This incident has shown that the Japanese warlords are determined to complete their plan to seize Chinese territory and turn Manchuria and North China into a training ground for future wars." (Tass dispatch on the 14th)

Not Allowing Interference from Third Countries

The Puppet State's Oil Monopoly: The United States Continues to Express Dissatisfaction 12

[Washington] Officials claimed today that although the quota for American oil imports into "Manchukuo" is higher than originally hoped, the officials are still dissatisfied. The United States' view is that although foreigners may be treated preferentially after the implementation of the monopoly, it must not make the monopoly reasonable. After this method is implemented, the United States may regard the matter as closed. (National News dispatch on the 14th)

Page 10

A Glimmer of Hope for Peace in Europe: Germany Endorses Air Defense Pact 13

Friendly Tone in Reply to British and French Governments, Reservations on Central and Eastern European Pact

[Geneva] World peace gained two major victories today. Germany has announced its complete acceptance of the terms of the British and French air defense plan. The League of Nations has also adopted the American proposal as the basis for future disarmament discussions. News from Rome and Berlin also indicates that Germany's response to the air pact expresses sympathy for the Italian-French agreement on non-interference in Austria. Only one matter seems less than perfect: Germany believes that Austria should be free to choose its own form of government, whether National Socialist or a restored monarchy. As for the Eastern Locarno Pact, Germany states that if its principles are based on military mutual assistance, then Germany opposes it. However, government authorities have already clarified that this pact is not a military alliance but a non-aggression agreement. It is noted that the German government's acceptance of the British and French air defense agreement was generally expected. It is reported that German Foreign Minister Neurath's reply to the British and French governments also stated that Germany is willing to discuss general disarmament issues. Semi-official sources say that the tone of the reply is very friendly and particularly satisfied with the cancellation of the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles. As for the League of Nations, the arms committee meeting here has passed the plan proposed by American representative Wilson to reopen the disarmament conference. Wilson had previously expressed that the United States strongly supports the British and French agreement. (14th National Telegram)

Main Points of German Reply 14

Oral Explanation by Neurath

[Berlin] Germany's response to the proposals in the British-French declaration of February 3rd was delivered this evening by Foreign Minister Neurath to the British and French ambassadors to Germany. The French ambassador, Poncet, immediately sent a translation to Paris. The reply was typed and consists of two pages, to be published in the newspapers on Saturday morning. It is said that the content is quite general in nature and expresses agreement, advocating the commencement of diplomatic talks to discuss the various proposals of the British and French governments. (14th Havas Telegram)

[London] Regarding the content of the German reply, very little is known here as of tonight. When German Foreign Minister Neurath delivered the reply to the British and French ambassadors, he attached an oral explanation, the content of which is also difficult to ascertain. According to initial reports, the tone of the reply is very moderate but deliberately vague, stating that Germany has good intentions and is willing to cooperate with all countries to achieve peace. Of the various proposals in the British-French declaration, Germany pays the most attention to the air pact. Germany has expressed acceptance of the principles and basis of the pact. As for the Danube Pact and the Eastern European mutual assistance pact plan, the reply does not seem to mention them. According to the British-French declaration, these two pacts must be implemented simultaneously before Germany's right to equal armament can be recognized and a general arms limitation treaty can be concluded to replace the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles. On this point, the German reply seems very ambiguous. (14th Havas Telegram)

[Berlin] Further details about the content of the German reply have been learned, which can be added to the above. Germany did not raise any questions about the British and French proposals but stated that the air pact proposal assumes that Germany is in an equal position in terms of armaments, which Germany has been constantly demanding. Now that the British and French governments have proposed concluding this pact, it is tantamount to tacitly acknowledging this right of equality. Regarding the draft Danube Pact, the German government generally believes that there is no need to restate its views in detail, so it only mentioned it in general terms in the reply. As for the Eastern European mutual assistance pact plan, its attitude is not as negative as the official newspapers have expressed, which is unexpected by most people. However, the German government believes that the issue of security can raise many problems, so it adopts a reserved attitude to avoid being constrained, but it does not refuse to jointly study the matter with the governments of the countries concerned. (14th Havas News Agency Telegram)

[Geneva] It is reported that Germany's reply to the air defense agreement stated that it is willing to entrust the German Air Force to the signatory countries of the air defense treaty for any joint action. Reliable sources explain that Germany has made this statement because the London agreement assumed that Germany already has this air force, but it cannot be regarded as Germany acknowledging that it has exceeded the scope stipulated by the Treaty of Versailles. (14th National Telegram)

[Paris] French Foreign Minister Laval studied the German reply immediately after receiving it. The reply was forwarded to France by the French ambassador to Germany. (15th National Telegram)

[Berlin] According to an article published in the Diplomatic Review, semi-official sources stated that the government's declaration is not surprising, as Germany has been striving to avoid any arms race and prevent the brewing of war in recent months. As for the document sent by Foreign Minister Neurath to the British and French ambassadors yesterday, the British communication contained only constructive elements, so there was no need to express acceptance or rejection. Furthermore, Germany is already negotiating on the security issues of Eastern and Southern Europe. Germany insists on exchanging views to resolve all difficulties. (15th National Telegram)

Disarmament Committee Meeting 15

Discussion of American Proposal

[Geneva] At today's meeting of the Disarmament Conference Committee to discuss the American draft convention on the suppression of arms trade and manufacturing, British representative Sir Stanhope expressed criticism of the American proposal to establish a permanent committee under the League of Nations to control arms trade and manufacturing, saying that it was too complicated and difficult to implement. The League's task is to enable countries to submit detailed reports on arms trade and manufacturing, not to monitor the number of guns and cannons manufactured. Therefore, the British government proposed that the League should make necessary inquiries and advocated adding a clause containing the principle that it is inconvenient to implement an export license system for arms trade, as this system would encourage countries to abuse funds on armaments. (14th Reuters Telegram)

[Geneva] The situation at today's meeting of the Disarmament Conference Committee on the Suppression of Arms Manufacturing and Trafficking, regarding the draft convention proposed by the United States, was better than yesterday. The representatives of various countries did not criticize the basic content of this proposal, and the representatives of Soviet Russia, Spain, Sweden, Belgium, Czechoslovakia, and Canada expressed their approval. Soviet Russian representative Antodorov believed that the American proposal allowed private manufacturing of arms, which was too broad in scope and inappropriate. He said that only Soviet Russia in the world can eliminate the evils of private arms manufacturing, because Russian arms manufacturing is entirely state-owned. However, although state-owned arms manufacturing is necessary, it cannot be implemented temporarily except for Soviet Russia. Therefore, the American proposal can be regarded as a reasonable compromise. American representative Wilson, the minister to Switzerland, stood up to thank everyone and reserved the right to reply to the various objections raised on the details. In addition, there is hope that the reservations raised by the British and Italian governments at yesterday's meeting will also be reduced. (15th Havas Telegram)

French Foreign Minister Laval Promotes Eastern European Pact 16

Three Meetings with Russian Ambassador

Guarantees "Diplomatic Check" Will Be Cashed

[Paris] Today, French Foreign Minister Laval spoke with Soviet Russian Ambassador Potemkin again. This is the third meeting in recent days, so it has attracted considerable attention from the outside world. It is generally believed that this is a resolute expression of Soviet Russian diplomatic policy, the purpose of which is to make France cash the "diplomatic check" issued by former Foreign Minister Barthou. As far as the outside world knows, what Soviet Russia requires is that France should adhere to a firm policy, so that when the negotiations on the Eastern European Pact fail on a broad basis, France's diplomatic policy will not waver. When Laval was previously in Geneva, he accepted the demands of the Little Entente countries and Soviet Russia. Since then, all actions have taken the negotiations on the Eastern European Pact as a prerequisite. Before the Eastern European Pact is established, no negotiations will be conducted with Germany. It is generally believed that he has reiterated his previous remarks in his recent talks with Potemkin. However, the official news released by the authorities is evasive on this point, only stating that Potemkin has been given the necessary repeated assurances and explanations. (14th National Telegram)

Prussian Governor Göring Expected to be Deputy Chancellor 17

[Berlin] Aviation Minister and Prussian Governor Göring will be appointed as Deputy Chancellor of Germany on March 1st. According to the law promulgated by the government on August 2, 1934, the day of the death of former President Marshal Hindenburg, Chancellor Hitler may elect a Deputy Chancellor, but this has been delayed until now due to domestic political reasons. It will be implemented simultaneously once the Saar returns to Germany. Recently, Göring has toured the provinces of Trieste and Bremen, and will soon go to the provinces of Bavaria and Württemberg, which shows that his political position is becoming increasingly important. U.S. Congress Approves National Defense Enhancement Plan 18

Shipbuilding Reaches Treaty Limits, Air Defense Strengthened, Army Mechanized

Former Air Force Commander Advocates Airship Policy

[Washington] Amid the enthusiastic expectations of the Big Navy and Continental Army factions, Congress, under the leadership of President Roosevelt, has fully agreed to the $2,000,000,000 national defense plan. This plan aims to make America's skies safe, protect America's coasts from enemy invasion, mechanize America's army, increase the number of servicemen, and bring America's naval power to treaty limits. (14th National Telegram)

[Washington] Former U.S. Air Force Commander Major General Mitchell declared today that America's abandonment of the airship policy is a symbol of spiritual degeneration. Mitchell told the House Licenses Committee today that the United States should continue to build large airships and make them the mainstay of American national defense. If we had fifty well-equipped Zeppelins, we could reach any country in Asia and destroy it. Mitchell has been very enthusiastic about all U.S. air defense matters since he was the commander of the U.S. Air Force stationed in France. Mitchell said that flying the Macon and other large airships over the fleet was a big mistake made by the Navy. To prevent airship accidents, the only way is to avoid storms and adverse weather conditions. The Macon had passed through storms twice before the accident, so its effectiveness was greatly reduced. Mitchell severely criticized the Navy for failing to have trained personnel to fly the Macon, and said that piloting large airships is as difficult as piloting ordinary ships, and the Navy should be aware of this. Large airships are ideal aircraft carriers, but they can also be used as offensive weapons, so they are even more valuable. I believe the United States should send young officers to the Zeppelin Company for training. Mitchell also suggested subsidizing the Goodyear Zeppelin Company, which built the Macon and Akron, to develop its business. (14th National Telegram)

U.S. Navy Begins Investigation into Cause of Macon Disaster 19

Probably Due to Weak Tail Structure

[Binghamton] The U.S. Navy Investigation Committee began investigating the cause of the U.S. Navy airship Macon disaster today. Commander Wund declared that when the Macon was flying off Point Sur at a speed of 63 knots at an altitude of 1,250 feet, he ordered the rudder to turn left, but shortly after, the whole ship shook, followed by an explosion. Before the accident, the ship was traveling through thick clouds, with rain below the clouds, and the ship was quite disturbed, so it descended from an altitude of 2,700 feet to 1,700 feet. The tail was damaged, and the ship crashed into the sea. He could not determine the cause of the tail gas balloon's damage. President Roosevelt stated today that there are no immediate plans to rebuild the airship. It is generally speculated that the Macon disaster was probably due to the weak tail structure. (14th Reuters Telegram)

Djibouti Port Controls the Vital Eurasian Transportation Route; Any Troops Passing Through Must Disarm; Italian Army Prepares to Depart; Ethiopian Government Lodges Protest

[Paris] With the dispute between Italy and Ethiopia, the French government has ordered the adoption of necessary precautions to avoid regrettable outcomes. The Ethiopian government has given favorable consideration to these requests. This order has been respectfully carried out by these soldiers. Until January 29, when Italian troops again attacked near the Gero Gebi area, the Ethiopian government reiterated its previous order, considering it a way to calm the situation. In Italy, after this offensive, it was announced that Afdubob, after Walwal, had been occupied by Italian troops. The Italian government's claim that Ethiopia has taken military measures, thus mobilizing two divisions, is unfounded. At a time when Italy and Ethiopia are conducting negotiations to form a committee to undertake reconciliation and arbitration, Italy's mobilization of two divisions runs counter to maintaining mutual trust, so that negotiations can be successfully completed." British House of Commons Debate Clarifies Political Atmosphere 23

Rumors of Cabinet Split Disappear

Unemployment Relief Bill Passes Both Houses

Labour Party's Motion of Impeachment Ultimately Defeated

[London] It is generally felt that yesterday's debate in the House of Commons has clarified the atmosphere. The remarks of Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain are particularly able to dispel the Conservative Party's split, reverse pessimism, and dispel speculation about a general election in the autumn. Dominion Minister Thomas gave a speech in London, firmly refuting the rumors of a government split and a general election soon to be held, saying that such rumors only cause disturbance and harm the people. Churchill declared inside and outside the House of Commons that his opposition to the government's Indian Bill was not due to any hostility towards the current government's organizational system, and he did not want to cause the Conservative Party to split. The Times said today that recent events have postponed the date of the general election, but it feels that there is still a need for a government reshuffle. The Manchester Guardian reported that Prime Minister MacDonald is gradually becoming the only public enemy of the cabinet, and the longer he remains at the helm, the heavier the cabinet will fall. (15th Reuters Telegram)

[London] The government's Unemployment Prevention Bill, after being passed by the House of Commons in the second reading, was passed by the House of Lords today. (14th Havas Telegram)

[London] At today's meeting of the House of Commons, Labour Party leader Lansbury moved a motion of impeachment against the government, accusing the government of failing to define any policy for the growing number of unemployed, and of deceiving Parliament on the financial impact of the regulations for maintaining the livelihood relief of the unemployed, thus losing the trust of the country. Lansbury said that what the Labour Party impeaches the government for is its inability to fulfill its duties. Everything that has happened has been foreseen by Labour Party members. Lansbury then attacked the household living test, calling it cruel and unparalleled. At this point, Dominion Minister Thomas intervened, saying that it was useless for Lansbury to compare today's test with the original method passed by the previous Labour government (of which Lansbury was also a member). Lansbury then said that unless the relief funds given to the unemployed are based on the best wage standards so that they can support themselves and their wives and children, the problem of unemployment will never be properly resolved. The leader of the "Samuel Liberal Party," Samuel, agreed that the government should be impeached, but said that all the mistakes that have occurred are due to the bureaucracy and serve as a warning to the Socialist Party in power. Then, female member Astor rose to speak, praising and criticizing both sides, and ultimately concluded that the Labour Party's policy was unworkable, advising the government not to surrender to this ragged army, witty remarks, and those who heard it laughed a lot. Finally, Prime Minister MacDonald rose to say that the emotions expressed by Lansbury were shared by all parties. He often believed that society must progress according to the law of evolution and cannot forcibly implement foreign revolutionary methods. If the opposition party can abandon criticism and cooperate with the government to find effective ways to deal with this problem, it would be of greater benefit. The government is willing to accept any truly constructive suggestions put forward by any party. The government is determined to return the unemployed to industry and become free and independent workers. Although he does not want to underestimate the importance of this issue, the national situation has indeed been improving recently. In recent days, there have been attempts to disturb people's minds and spread various rumors, indicating that the government is about to step down, which is actually for other purposes. The Prime Minister then cited a trade report stating that Britain's exports in January increased by more than 12%, and the steel industry in 1934 was better than it had been since 1930, saying that these were all good signs. The government's entire policy, especially its financial policy, has won the trust of the industrial world, which has led to new plans, the result of which has enabled a large number of unemployed to find work. When the Prime Minister gave his speech, he was repeatedly interrupted by the Labour Party, and the Speaker had to intervene to restore order. After the Prime Minister finished his speech, Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain spoke to end the debate, saying that the government's policy on unemployment relief was very effective. The government's refusal to spend huge amounts of money on public works was because it had to use this fee to promote ordinary trade. He expected that the recent increase in the number of unemployed would soon find jobs. The number of workers currently employed has increased by 700,000 compared to three years ago. The policies proposed by Britain or any other country cannot be compared with what this government has achieved. The government's various plans to restore export trade are gradually succeeding. The government does not want to abandon cheap currency and maintain a stable financial policy, because the continued effectiveness of the policy to reduce unemployed workers will only rely on this. After the debate, Lansbury's motion was put to a vote and defeated by a vote of 374 to 68. (14th Reuters Telegram)

Japanese Upper House Member Advocates Changing to Silver Standard 24

On Sino-Japanese Economic Cooperation

Foreign Ministry Studies Concrete Plan

[Tokyo] The Upper House held its first general accounting meeting at 1:44 p.m. today. Ryutaro Fukao (Koseikai) advocated that Japan abolish the gold standard and adopt the silver standard, and said that I have always opposed Manchuria's silver standard being changed to the gold standard, and I also oppose Japan's gold standard. I am gratified to hear that Finance Minister Takahashi also believes that it is not the time. I also believe that the currencies of China, Japan, and Manchuria must be unified, but I do not agree with the gold standard, and I advocate that Japan's gold standard be changed to the silver standard. Why should Japan adopt the same currency system as Europe and the United States? The fluctuation of silver prices is not necessarily frequent, and it sometimes fluctuates due to changes in gold prices. The price index in China has not changed much, which proves that the silver standard can be unimpeded. Therefore, I advocate that Japan voluntarily change to the silver standard and cooperate with China and Manchuria to form a silver group of the three countries. Finance Minister Takahashi replied to this by saying that I oppose Manchuria's abolition of the silver standard, and it seems that the Manchurian authorities do not have this intention either. I am not in a position to answer clearly about the theory of Japan changing to the silver standard. Fukao reiterated that he hoped that the authorities would work hard to unify the currency system in order to form a silver group of the three countries as soon as possible. (15th United Press Telegram)

[Tokyo] The opportunity for Sino-Japanese economic cooperation has become increasingly strong. The Foreign Ministry has been holding consultations for days to study concrete plans. The Foreign Ministry authorities have the following general views on this: The fundamental problem of Sino-Japanese economic cooperation is to eradicate the anti-Japanese movement in China. China's self-reliance is the most important thing. If China hopes to do so, it will not hesitate to provide technical assistance. In order to improve China's trade deficit, it is essential to import cheap Japanese goods in place of expensive European and American goods. If China actively improves Sino-Japanese trade and requests loans for settlement, it should fully consider appropriate measures. In order to revitalize China's cotton and other agriculture, it is urgent for Japan to provide technical assistance to restore China's economy and increase the purchasing power of the people. (15th Den-tsu Telegram)

After Death Sentence, Hoffmman Weeps All Night in Jail 25

Lawyers Launch Fundraising Campaign to Prepare for Appeal

Mother Petitions President to Pardon Her Son's Death Sentence

Flemington – Today, the lawyer Reilly for Hauptmann, who was sentenced to death yesterday in Flemington, launched a fundraising appeal to save Mr. Hauptmann's life. He also claimed that he would request a stay of execution to allow for an appeal. Today, he will meet with Mr. Hauptmann to discuss the appeal. If the court does not allow the appeal, he will seek relief from the Court of Errors and Appeals. If the request for a reduced sentence is not approved, he will appeal to the Pardon Court, which is scheduled to convene in October. Mr. Hauptmann's mother in Germany has written to President Roosevelt, asking him to pardon her son's death sentence. Mr. Hauptmann has been weeping all night in jail, still claiming his innocence. It is reported that Mr. Hauptmann will be moved to the death row in Trenton, New Jersey tomorrow. It is now known that the jury voted six times before deciding on the death penalty. One male juror named Clava, a conservative education leader in New Jersey, voted five times that Mr. Hauptmann was guilty but advocated for leniency. Two female jurors also initially advocated for commuting Mr. Hauptmann's death sentence on the first vote but changed their position on the second vote and convicted Mr. Hauptmann of first-degree murder. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

Flemington – After being sentenced to death, Hauptmann was disheartened and refused to eat, only smoking. Clergymen offered him the Bible, but he refused to accept it. It is reported that after the sentencing, Hauptmann fainted when he was taken back to his cell. When he woke up, he was nervous and agitated. Fearing that he would commit suicide, the jailers are now closely monitoring him. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

Flemington – The local prison has allowed journalists to visit Bruno Hauptmann, the suspect in the Lindbergh baby kidnapping and murder case, for the first time. Hauptmann told reporters, "If I must die in the electric chair, I will face it calmly." When asked if there was anything to confess, he replied, "If I had anything to confess, I would have done so months ago so that my wife and son would not suffer. I am penniless and cannot afford an appeal. If the public does not help me, I will ask my lawyer to appeal for me." (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

International Business Telegraph

Exclusive Business News from Reuters on February 15

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: The London gold price today is 142 shillings and 8.5 pence, up 2 pence.

London Silver: The London silver price today is 24.8125 pence for spot and 24.9375 pence for futures, both up 0.1875. Purchases from India and China, with few sellers. The closing market was stable.

Exchange Rates

British-American: In the London foreign exchange market this morning, there was a slight demand for both US dollars and francs, with minimal price fluctuations. The opening exchange rate for British-American was $4.876875, which is 0.0625 lower than the last closing price. It rose by 0.0625 at 11:00 am, but fell back to the opening price at noon, and remained unchanged until 2:00 pm.

British-French: The opening price was 73.96 francs, the same as the last closing price. It fell by 0.06 at 11:00 am to 73.90. It fell again by 0.06 at 2:00 pm to 73.84 francs, which is the latest price.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened slightly higher, with purchases from traders, but it seemed to lack momentum.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was firmer this morning. At 1:00 pm, the May futures price was 6.77, up 0.03 from yesterday's close. British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was slightly lower. At 1:00 pm, the May futures price was 4 shillings and 10.75 pence, down 0.0375 from yesterday's close.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened quietly today, with prices remaining stable. Although it opened lower, the drop was minimal and insignificant.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market was stable at the opening this morning but turned quiet at noon. The trading price for July and September was 6.6875 pence, the same as yesterday's close.

New York: The New York rubber market opened quietly but trended slightly upward later, due to the satisfactory consumption figures for January.

Securities

New York: The Wall Street market today remained stagnant and lifeless. The opening prices were similar to yesterday's close, but there was slightly more activity later, and sentiment turned firmer. Three Agencies Review Speculation in Cotton Yarn 27

[Nanjing] On the 15th, the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Finance, Ministry of Industry, Economic Commission, and Cotton Industry Control Committee jointly reviewed the case of cracking down on speculation in cotton yarn at the exchange. The meeting adjourned at 11:00 am. As a result, a principle for cracking down was drafted and submitted to the Executive Yuan for discussion and decision. (Special dispatch on the 15th)

[Nanjing] According to the request of the cotton spinning industry, the Shanghai General Labor Union stated that the Chinese Yarn and Cloth Exchange opened both yarn and cotton auctions simultaneously, leading speculators to knowingly raise prices and hoard supplies despite domestic cotton production being insufficient. Most domestic yarn factories have exhausted their capital and have no ability to purchase goods, resulting in a situation of expensive cotton and cheap yarn. They requested the establishment of relief measures to maintain the yarn industry and workers' livelihoods. According to the person in charge of the Ministry of Industry, they are currently discussing with the Ministry of Finance to find ways to maintain the balance between the prices of yarn and cotton auctions at the exchange, and whether to stop the cotton auctions will depend on the actual situation. According to archaeologists at the Lushun Museum, the beast lived 15,000 to 20,000 years ago, was approximately six feet tall, and had a total length of eighteen feet from head to tail. (Reuters dispatch on the 15th)
