"War Zone" Clearance Committee Decides on Clearance Procedures 95

Important Chinese and Japanese Figures Exchange Views at the Yin Residence; The Japanese Side Understands the New Peace Preservation Corps; Umezu, Isogu, and Others to Inspect Chahar and Suiyuan

Beijing Correspondence: The "war zone" clearance issue, which has been stalled for nearly half a year, has recently been brought up again for negotiations. Doihara, the head of the Kwantung Army Special Service Agency in Shenyang, recently came to Peiping and Tianjin and separately convened responsible representatives from both sides to exchange views. Doihara has now left Tianjin and headed south. Important figures from both sides, such as Iwai (representative of the Kwantung Army), Oki (representative of the Japanese Garrison in Tianjin), Takahashi (military attaché of the Japanese Embassy), as well as Yin Tong, Yin Rugeng, Tao Shangming, and others, came to Peiping together yesterday (the 13th) afternoon at around 6 PM and continued the meeting at the Yin residence in Dongzongbu Hutong. According to reliable sources, a concrete decision has been generally reached regarding the "war zone" clearance issue as a result of discussions between the representatives of both sides. However, regarding the implementation steps, the Japanese side indicated that the Chinese side can decide and respond. The "War Zone" Clearance Committee then held a meeting at the West Building of the Political Reorganization Committee this afternoon (the 14th) at 3 PM. Standing Committee members Yin Tong and Zhu Shiqin, as well as committee members Yin Rugeng, Tao Shangming, Yue Kaixian, and Xu Tongxin, attended on time. The committee members conducted a thorough discussion on the issue. After an hour, the implementation procedures were decided, and the meeting adjourned at 4:30 PM. Yin Tong has scheduled to officially respond to the Japanese side tomorrow (the 15th) to actively begin the clearance work. The reporter met Yin Tong at a certain place this afternoon (the 14th). According to him, "Although a concrete result has been achieved with the Japanese side regarding the 'war zone' issue, there are still many matters that need further discussion before implementation. What I can briefly tell you is that the Japanese side has understood the matter of the newly organized Peace Preservation Corps entering the war zone. The number is agreed upon to be around 9,000, including 4,000 police officers, carrying light weapons, and the Japanese side has no objection. This matter can be realized after another round of negotiations. Secondly, regarding the issue of receiving the Eastern Tombs of Malanyu, we must wait for Takahashi Tan, the military attaché of the Japanese Embassy, to go to Changchun next month, report to Nanjirō, the commander of the Japanese Kwantung Army, and return to Peiping before further discussions can be conducted." Yin stated solemnly, "The 'war zone' issue was virtually suspended due to certain reasons in the past. In order to bring the 'war zone' clearance work to a conclusion as soon as possible, our side requested continued discussions with the Japanese side. Recently, the voices of improving Sino-Japanese relations have been rising, so the 'war zone' issue has also had the opportunity to be resolved smoothly. The future, whether smooth or not, depends on the efforts of all parties."

Several important Japanese figures who have come to Peiping in recent days include Iwai, Oki, and Umezu Mijirō, the commander of the Japanese Garrison in Tianjin, who arrived in Peiping this afternoon (the 14th), as well as Isogu, the newly appointed Japanese military attaché to Shanghai. He Yingqin, the chairman of the Military Council, hosted a banquet at Jurenhall this evening (the 14th) to welcome them in order to fulfill the hospitality of the host. He also invited Japanese military attaché Takahashi, as well as Yin Tong, Yin Rugeng, Tao Shangming, Zhu Shiqin, Yue Kaixian, and others to accompany them. The atmosphere was lively, and the guests and hosts dispersed in enjoyment at around 9 PM. Umezu came to Peiping to study Japanese academia in North China and plans to go to Datong to view the Yungang Grottoes project before inspecting Chahar and Suiyuan. Zhu Zheyuan, the chairman of Chahar, instructed Qin Decun, the Director of the Civil Affairs Department, by telegram from Tianjin to return to Zhangjiakou from Peiping at 3:30 PM this afternoon (the 14th) to prepare for hospitality matters in order to properly host him. Isogu was originally the director of the Second Department of the Japanese General Staff Headquarters. Recently, due to the transfer of the military attaché to Shanghai to his home country, he was appointed to succeed him. He will first go to Peiping and Tianjin, then inspect Chahar and Suiyuan before going to Shanghai to take office. When he passes through Nanjing, he will meet with our officials. As for the future whereabouts of Iwai and Oki, it is learned that Oki will return to Tianjin in the coming days, and Iwai will go directly to Changchun from Peiping to report everything to Nanjirō.

According to general observations, the "war zone" issue can be brought to a conclusion within the next two months. After Yin Tong responds to the Japanese side on the implementation steps of our clearance tomorrow (the 15th), if necessary, he will go south to meet with Huang Fu in person to report the negotiations with the Japanese side. Tao Shangming has been away from Tangshan for a long time. According to reports, he plans to return to Tangshan the day after tomorrow (the 16th) to manage government affairs. As for the actual implementation period of the clearance work, in fact, it may begin at the beginning of next month. In short, since the issue of the troop rotation of the New Peace Preservation Corps in the "war zone" can be resolved, other issues may be easier to find a solution. (14th)

Sichuan: After the Establishment of the New Provincial Government 96

Liu Xiang Issues Earnest Instructions to County Magistrates

Integrity Should Be the Foundation of Politics

Chongqing Correspondence: Sichuan's politics have not been on the right track due to the fact that the defense zones have not been broken for many years. Now that the Sichuan bandits are gradually being suppressed, Liu Xiang, the Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression, has been ordered to preside over provincial administration. Various armies have handed over their power to the government. Liu is known for his integrity, and Sichuan's administration is expected to improve. Since the new provincial government was established on the 10th of this month, the work has been quite tense. Liu arrives at the provincial government early every morning to handle important official matters. The directors of various departments and the secretary-general arrive on time to work diligently. Liu also believes that clean governance is paramount for officials close to the people, so that the people can live and work in peace. Yesterday, he issued a notice to all counties, earnestly admonishing and warning them to strive for improvement, strictly prohibiting petty annoyances to the people, and put forward three key points to instruct them on cultivating the people and being honest in office, which are extremely pertinent. The original text is as follows: "It is hereby noted that modern politics emphasizes efficiency the most. Since the establishment of this government, it is urgent to implement government orders and govern effectively. According to our country's administrative divisions, the county is an important unit. County administration must be substantial in order for the entire administration to have a foundation. I hereby highlight the key points to indicate the political goals. First, recognize the mission of the times. Governments and officials are established for the people, and their position is that of public servants. Approaching the masses is their duty, and serving the people is their responsibility. Loyalty and diligence are only fulfilling one's duties, and there is no so-called meritorious administration. County magistrates should recognize their own positions and should go deep among the people, diligently seek the people's stability, and inspect on time as a fixed routine. Private visits are only accidental, while pacifying the people is a divine duty. From now on, implement being close to the people and strictly prohibit petty annoyances. This is the first point that should be earnestly warned. Second, be realistic. In recent years, the political system has been uneven, and laws and regulations have been complicated. Those who are careful are troubled by coping, and those who are clever use it as an excuse to make a fuss. Now that provincial administration is centralized, it is precisely to take simplicity. Since county magistrates have reduced the burden of paperwork, they should focus their energy on reality. It must be known that official documents are a manifestation of official affairs, and official affairs are not just official documents. From now on, the chairman will evaluate political achievements based solely on reality and will never rank them based on official documents. County magistrates should strive for improvement and not take a passive approach to save trouble. If they only follow the form, it is merely seeking temporary peace and being opportunistic. Without sincerity, there is nothing. Deceiving the people is deceiving oneself. This is the second point that should be earnestly warned. Third, hone one's integrity. The Six Strategies emphasize integrity, and the Three Admonitions emphasize incorruptibility. It is a common meaning throughout history that integrity is the foundation of politics. It must be that one is not casual about trivial matters so that one can be free from shame. At this time of financial exhaustion and popular impoverishment, with the upper and lower classes in difficulty, and seeing the suffering of the people, how can one bear to enrich oneself? In recent years, the meaning of popular governance has flourished greatly. Private wealth must also be restrained. If one cleverly seizes the people's wealth, it is going against the natural order. Heaven is impartial and will not allow self-preservation. County magistrates who receive salaries are all supported by the people. To hold a position without doing anything is already shameful, let alone being corrupt. This is the third point that should be earnestly warned. The above three points are not only the common meaning of serving as an official but also the ordinary virtues of life. The chairman will use this to evaluate performance and is determined to implement it. After this admonition, the county magistrates should be mindful of the difficulties of the times, be diligent in caring for the people's suffering, and strive to arouse their conscience and earnestly practice them. If the government is clear and bright, the achievements of governance will have a foundation. Today, the people are in dire straits and need to be saved. If there is a little good governance, there will be celebrations of their well-being. The proverb says that it is easy to be a good official in chaotic times, which is truly a well-considered statement. The chairman earnestly admonishes and is straightforward without concealment. If anyone dares to be negligent, he will be immediately dismissed. Those who are corrupt with evidence will be severely punished if the people accuse them and it is found to be true or if the government discovers it. There will be no leniency. This order is to be promulgated immediately, and you are to abide by it respectfully. This is the order." (Guowen News Agency)

Japanese Ronin in Qingdao Selling Certificates for Entry into the Puppet State 97

Municipal Government Sends Letter to Japanese Consulate Requesting Crackdown

Qingdao Correspondence: Last September, Japanese ronin once established the "Great East Company" at the Qingdao Dagaan Wharf, selling certificates for entry into the puppet state of Manchuria. The municipal government filed a protest with the Japanese Consul in Qingdao, and the Japanese Consulate sent police to crack down, and the company had already disappeared without a trace. Unexpectedly, after several months, the company suddenly reappeared, openly posting notices and selling certificates for entry into the puppet state of Manchuria, priced at one yuan each. It officially opened on the 12th of this month, with the office located on Xinjiang Road in Dagaan. A notice posted outside the gate stated: "Notice: For the convenience of those entering Manchuria and to save expenses, this company has established free lodging for Chinese workers in Xinjing, Fengtian, Dalian, Andong, Yingkou, and other places. It specializes in providing vocational introductions, negotiations, and assistance for illnesses and disasters for those entering Manchuria, without charging any fees. Those entering Manchuria are requested to pay attention to this. Detailed information can be obtained at this office." The company also notified various shipping companies that all Chinese workers traveling to Manchuria from Qingdao by ship must carry the pseudo-state certificate sold by the company, otherwise, in addition to the person not being allowed to land, the shipping company would bear considerable responsibility upon arrival. When the No. 16 Kyodo Maru left on the 13th, a large number of Chinese workers boarded the ship to go to the Eastern Provinces to make a living, all carrying the pseudo-state certificate. They were discovered by the guards at the Dagaan Wharf, who reported it to the Dagaan Police Station, detaining 102 people. By this time, 125 people had already boarded the ship and could not be stopped. It was found that these Chinese workers were all farmers from various counties in the Shandong interior. Due to rural bankruptcy, they were unable to make a living and were taking advantage of the spring warmth to go to the Northeast to make a living. Since they were detained by the Public Security Bureau, they could neither go nor return, and they wandered near the Dagaan Wharf and refused to leave. The Public Security Bureau reported this situation to the municipal government. In addition to ordering the Public Security Bureau to send these farmers back to their original places, the municipal government sent many plainclothes police officers to spread throughout the wharf, intercepting anyone holding the pseudo-state certificate. It also sent a letter to the Japanese Consulate for serious negotiations, requesting that they strictly crack down. Therefore, when the Fengtian Maru departed on the 14th, no one was allowed to leave. However, the company, fearing that it would be affected by the intervention of our officials, also sent several Japanese policemen to patrol near the wharf. The Japanese policemen went to the police station and questioned them. The patrol officer replied that it was being done under orders from above. The Japanese policemen left reluctantly. The attitude of the Japanese Consul towards this matter is not yet known. (15th)

Local Reorganization of the Shanxi Provincial Government 98

—Changes of Provincial Committee and Various Officials—

Taiyuan Correspondence: There have been slight adjustments among the members of the Shanxi Provincial Government recently. One is Wang Maogong's resignation from the Provincial Committee, one is Lu Jinli's resignation from his concurrent position as Director of the Department of Construction while also serving on the Provincial Committee, and one is Geng Buchan's reassignment while also serving on the Provincial Committee and Director of the Department of Industry, with the Department of Industry being fundamentally abolished. The affairs handled by the Department of Industry are merged into the Department of Construction, and all of Geng's concurrent positions are dismissed. It is found that Wang Maogong was originally the Director of the Zhengtai Railway Bureau. The reason why he concurrently served on the Provincial Committee was simply to facilitate the nearby transmission of the intentions of the Central Government and the Shanxi Provincial Government, remotely leading in name only. Wang only attended the Provincial Government meetings once or twice at the beginning of his term and never inquired about provincial affairs. He resigned from the Zhengtai Railway Bureau a month ago because he was unsuited to the northern climate and often suffered from illness. The position of Shanxi Provincial Committee was naturally unable to be remotely held for a long time. Lu Jinli, the Director of the Department of Construction, had once served as the Director of the Tianjin Customs Office after being relieved of his duties due to the changes in the political situation in the north in 1911. After more than a year, due to the complexity of his duties and the difficulty of finance, he firmly requested to resign. The authorities retained him without success and changed him to serve as the Director of the Department of Construction. Lu still had a one-year term, and by the end of last winter, the term expired and he again firmly resigned and no longer went to the department to handle affairs. It is heard that Lu's intention is to abandon his official career and engage in industry and make other contributions. In addition, Lu is a financial expert in Shanxi Province. This time, he was only allowed to resign from the position of Director of the Department, and the title of Provincial Committee member was still retained, and the authorities relied on him and did not let him get rid of it. Geng Buchan, who served concurrently as Director of the Department of Industry, once served as Director of the Department of Industry when Shanxi was first established in 1927. He went into retirement in 1930 when the Shanxi situation changed. Later, Yan Xishan returned to Shanxi, and Geng took over the Department of Industry for the second time. The reason for the abolition of the Department of Industry this time is that Yan has set a ten-year construction plan for provincial administration and established the Northwest Industrial Company to actively carry out. All industrial matters in the province are handled by the company, and what remains is only a very simple administrative surface article, and it is naturally unnecessary to set up a special department. Yan attaches great importance to the Northwest Industrial Company in recent times, and the promotion of the ten-year construction plan will be based on this as a source. Various factories and other public utilities set up by the company have been established one after another and expanded in turn. Recently, Liang Ruzhou (now renamed Hangbiao), the former Director of the Xingying Office, was appointed as the general manager, responsible for planning everything. Although Liang has repeatedly refused, he has agreed to take office after Yan's persuasion. Liang is the backbone of the newly advanced faction in Yan's staff. His appointment to this important position will help Yan's industrial construction. The vacancies of Wang and Geng on the Provincial Committee have now been filled, one by Fan Xiangli, the former Vice Minister of the Ministry of Internal Affairs and current Director of the Village Administration Office of the Shanxi Provincial Government, and the other by Wang Xiang, the current Director of the Shanxi Provincial Bank. Wang also concurrently serves as the Director of the Department of Construction. Wang was originally a member of the academic community and gained fame for running the Provincial No. 1 Middle School in the early years of the Republic of China, which is still praised by people today. In the past two years, he has made great achievements in sorting out the bank's business and has suddenly assumed his current position. The vacancy of the bank manager left by Wang has been filled by Wang Qian, the current Secretary-General of the Provincial Government. The vacancy of the Secretary-General of the Provincial Government will be filled by Li Naijing, the current Director of the Opium Suppression Assessment Office. In addition, Geng Buchan, the relieved Director of the Department of Industry, has been appointed by Yan as a senior advisor to the Suiyuan Appeasement Office. This is a scene of recent ups and downs in the Shanxi situation. (February 9)

Ten Provinces Including Hubei and Henan Prohibit Opium: Each Sets Up Supervisory Commissioners 99

Trial Implementation in Hubei Province First, Then Extended to Other Provinces

Crackdown on Opium Cultivation and Elimination of Other Narcotics

Hankou Correspondence: Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, in order to eliminate opium and other narcotics, issued an order to ten provinces, including Hubei, Henan, Anhui, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang, to strictly prohibit opium, and established an Opium Prohibition Supervisory Office in Hankou, with Li Jihong as the director, presiding over everything. In order to effectively promote opium prohibition, the office decided to implement a supervisory system. Each province and special municipality will establish an opium prohibition supervisory commissioner, and each county and city will establish supervisors, responsible for handling matters. The plan has been submitted to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek for approval, and will be implemented in Hubei province first, followed by others. The supervisory matters to be carried out by the supervisory commissioners are seven in number: (1) prohibit the cultivation of opium seedlings and eliminate highly toxic narcotics; (2) crack down on the number and level of opium paste shops and issue licenses with the number of users filled in; (3) matters relating to the seizure of narcotics in various counties and cities; (4) matters relating to opium prohibition statistical books and forms; (5) assessment of the performance of opium dens in various counties and cities; (6) matters assigned by order; (7) making recommendations to the Opium Prohibition Supervisory Office and directing supervisors in various counties and cities to carry out supervisory matters. The tasks of supervisors in various counties and cities are roughly the same. The Hubei provincial supervisory commissioners will be appointed by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and will be supervised and directed by the Opium Prohibition Supervisory Office. The list of candidates is still to be decided. The county and city inspectors will be appointed by the Opium Prohibition Supervisory Office in accordance with the jurisdiction of the administrative supervisory district, namely: Ye Guangyong in the First District, Lin Gongren in the Second District, Yang Runnong in the Third District, Cheng Wuchang in the Fourth District, Peng Yigan in the Fifth District, Mi Jinglin in the Sixth District, Li Songxian in the Seventh District, Che Zhiwen in the Eighth District, He Fuzhou in the Ninth District, Wang Yue in the Tenth District, and Zhang Gu in the Eleventh District. A letter has been sent to the provincial government today to instruct the administrative commissioners and county magistrates of various districts to assist in the process. (14th)

松江 100

Passenger Jumps into River and Commits Suicide

At Fengjia Ferry outside the South Gate, on the afternoon of the thirteenth, an unidentified man crossed the river from north to south. When the boat was in the middle of the river, he suddenly jumped into the water. The boatmen Feng Qinfa and Feng Guiqin tried their best to rescue him, but he was already barely breathing and unable to speak. After a few minutes, he died. The case was reported to the court's prosecutor's office, which dispatched Prosecutor Liu Shanjun with bailiff Han Mingzhong, coroner Wang Jian, and others yesterday to examine the body. The deceased was about thirty years old, wearing a dark-colored cotton padded jacket and trousers, and a blue cloth apron. There were no injuries on the body, confirming that he had jumped into the river and committed suicide. An order was issued for the local police to take custody of the body at the Cangfen Altar, and a notice was posted to identify the deceased.

Youth Attempts Suicide by Poisoning, Rescued

Tu Xiuzai, a 25-year-old youth from Suzhou, previously worked as a jacquard pattern technician at a textile factory in Wuxian County. Due to the factory's closure, he lost his job and came to Shanghai to seek employment without success. Running out of money, he walked to Songjiang, but having no relatives or friends, he became despondent. He ingested raw opium and lay down under the eaves of the Caishen Temple in Yangjia Bridge within the city. The police discovered him and took him to the First Precinct, then transferred him to the hospital for treatment, where he was revived. Officer Lu then bought him a train ticket back to his hometown to prevent him from wandering in a foreign land.

Suzhou 101

Treasury Department Strictly Pursues Old Taxes

Since 1927, Wuxian County has accumulated 680,000 yuan in back taxes, with the Dongting East and West Mountains owing the most, about 200,000 yuan. The Treasury Department has specially dispatched tax collection commissioner Guo Fupei to Suzhou to discuss collection methods with the county government. The deadline is from February to the end of June. If the taxes are not paid by the deadline, the defaulting households will be detained, or their property will be seized.

Taicang 102

Death Caused by Excessive Drinking

Hu Yunxiang, a 53-year-old villager from near Lu Yigong Temple north of Banqiao outside the East Gate of this county, drank excessively at the East Gate the day before yesterday. Returning home at night, he carried a lamp, which caught fire, burning his clothes. In his drunken stupor, he did not notice, and the fire spread to his whole body, burning him to death near the north end of Banqiao. The next day, passersby discovered the body. His family claimed the body for burial. Furthermore, Yan Zhongmou, a 45-year-old villager residing near Guanjia Bridge in Chaihang Township outside the East Gate, gambled with friends after drinking, losing all his money. He had long harbored a grudge against his relatives and feared being scolded upon returning home. Therefore, at about 4 a.m. that morning, he hastily went to the river near Guanjia Bridge and drowned himself. After the body was discovered, it was retrieved and prepared for burial.

Wuxi 103

Citywide Strike Calmed

The Public Security Bureau and the Fire Brigade in this county clashed over gambling arrests, resulting in the destruction of the North Section Fire Brigade and the Fifth Branch of the Public Security Bureau. The Public Security Bureau also detained and beat firefighters, which triggered a citywide strike. The police also briefly went on strike, causing widespread panic and chaos. After the Party and government officials made every effort to mediate, the strike gradually subsided. It is said that the strike was caused by the Public Security Bureau Chief Chen Yuchu's abrupt handling of affairs, which gave the public a very bad impression, causing public resentment to boil over and nearly become uncontrollable. Fortunately, County Magistrate Yan Shenyu, together with the Party headquarters and local figures, properly mediated the situation, which was resolved without incident. Yesterday (the 15th) morning, all the stores in the city resumed business, and social order was restored. Public Security Bureau Chief Chen Yuchu's family packed up and returned to Hangzhou on the day of the incident. Hong Houchang, chief of the Fifth Branch of the Public Security Bureau, Gu Songdong, a bureau member, and all the staff, as well as Tong Zhongyue, chief of the Third Branch, and Ling Guangyuan, patrol officer of the Seventh Sub-station, all resigned.

Another Fire in Cotton Alley

The home of Chen Daguan, resident of No. 49 Cotton Alley outside the West Gate, consisted of four sections of single-story buildings. Jiang Qingyun Lumber Yard was to the west of the house. Chen had two young sons and a daughter. Yesterday (the 15th) morning around 10 a.m., the children were playing with fire in the fourth section, causing a fire to break out. Soon, flames burst through the roof. Residents nearby immediately rang gongs to raise the alarm. Fire brigades One and Two of the West District, upon hearing the alarm, immediately rushed to the scene and tried their best to extinguish the fire. As a result, the fourth section of the house was completely burned down. Although the first, second, and third sections were not affected, many parts were damaged due to the rescue efforts. The total loss is estimated at 500-600 yuan.

Robbery with Injury in Tianxian Port

In Fan Alley, Tianxian Port, about three li north of Zhangjing Bridge in this county, there are more than a dozen households, mostly farmers. The day before yesterday (the 14th) around 11 p.m., more than thirty robbers suddenly came to the home of Lu Xingquan in the village, broke down the door, and threatened them to silence. They tied Xingquan to a long bench with rope, poured lime water down his throat, and forced him to reveal the location of the hidden silver. Xingquan nearly died three times before revealing that the collected association money was hidden in the mud of the pigsty. The robbers, upon hearing this, rushed to search, and as a result, more than 700 yuan was robbed. The robbers were not satisfied and went to Lu Jinbao's house to rob, also stealing 18 yuan in silver dollars, five dan of white rice, and clothing. Fortunately, no one was injured. Before leaving, they set off three firecrackers to show their power. The two victims have reported the losses to the county bureau and requested an investigation.

Jiangyin 104

High Court Thoroughly Investigates Bribery Case of Warden

Hu A-yu, a morphine dealer from Qingyang, was detained in the county last year and sentenced to two years in prison and a fine of 200 yuan by Judge Shi Cheng. He was imprisoned. It was reported that Hu faked illness and asked someone to bail him out. Someone accused the High Court, pointing to Chen Shusheng, the former warden (from Wangting, Suzhou), and Huang Youbo, the former town leader of Sihetangtou Bridge, along with villagers Qian Rongbing and Xue Gengshen, of defrauding 1,000 yuan in bribes to influence Judges Zhu and Qian of the High Court to help him. The High Court, based on the accusation, considered the case involved bribery and the reputation of the court, and ordered the Jiangyin County Government to summon Huang Youbo and others to court on the 13th to question Hu A-yu. Huang Youbo and others strongly denied the allegations. Questioning Hu A-yu, he also firmly denied it. Statements were recorded and submitted to the High Court for review.

Zhenjiang 105

Eight-Year-Old Child Dies Under Wheels

Around 4 p.m. on the 14th, a car No. 262 of the Zhonghua Road Xinzhen Automobile Company was returning to the city from Zhulin Temple with passengers. While driving on the Zhongzheng Road at the Louxiang intersection, an eight-year-old child named Liu Layuezi was on the roadside and failed to avoid the car. Letter to the Editor - From Qian Xijin 106

To the Editor:

I have read the news in your esteemed newspaper on the 11th of this month regarding the disappearance of the director of the Heyang Agricultural Education Center in Changshu, which has caused me great astonishment. I, Qian Xijin, reported and wrote off the public funds accounts, etc., during my tenure at the County Library in the past year, and reported the handover situation to the Education Bureau together with Mr. Cai. As for the false accusation that I, Qian Xijin, have embezzled all the public accumulation fund, it will be clear upon inquiry with the Education Bureau. Later, I was ordered to be transferred to the Taihe Agricultural Education Center for consolidation, and the department ordered the appointment of the director of the better performing center of the two centers, so I was appointed to my current position. The evidence is still there and is not difficult to verify. At the time when our center is holding the annual custom exhibition, it is said that I suddenly disappeared, and the staff has asked the Education Bureau for instructions, etc., which I do not know what it refers to. This rumor is obviously for other purposes. As it concerns my personal reputation, I specially request the editor to correct it. I am grateful and wish you well.

Sincerely,

Qian Xijin, Director of the Heyang Agricultural Education Center, Changshu County.

Special Envoy Huang Musong Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday to Comfort and Console Tibet 107

Says Tibetan People Enthusiastically Support the Central Government

Will Go to Beijing Within Days to Report to the Central Government

Mr. Huang Musong, the special envoy dispatched by the Central Government to Tibet to offer sacrifices to the late Dalai Lama, returned to China via India last winter. He arrived in Hong Kong at the beginning of the month and took a short trip to Guangdong Province. He returned to Shanghai yesterday morning at 10:30 a.m. on the Queen of Asia from Hong Kong. After disembarking, Mr. Huang went to the Zhou Dou Restaurant to rest and is scheduled to go to Beijing today or tomorrow to report everything to the Central Government. Details are as follows:

Welcoming Personnel

According to the Central News Agency, those who went to the Gonghexiang Wharf to welcome him yesterday included: Li Dachao, representative of the Municipal Government; Xu Jinyuan, representative of the Songhu Garrison Commander; Lieutenant General Liu Zhilu; Zeng Yangfu, Director of the Zhejiang Construction Department; Guo Weiping, Staff Officer of the Border Affairs Group of the National Government's General Staff; Xie Zhongfu, Member of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee; Pan Dajing, Executive of the Northwest Problem Research Association; Li Yuxuan, Li Fengwu, and Gu Yuhui, representatives of the Guangdong Native Place Association in Shanghai; Aisa, former Secretary of the Xinjiang Construction Committee; as well as the Tibetan Office in Beijing, the Jiaying Five Prefectures Native Place Association, and more than 50 relatives and friends of Special Envoy Huang. The Guangdong Native Place Association and the Jiaying Five Prefectures Native Place Association representatives all held flags welcoming Special Envoy Huang.

Arrival Situation

The ship entered the port at 9 a.m. and arrived at the Gonghexiang Wharf at 10 a.m. All the welcoming personnel gathered at the wharf to wait. After docking, Special Envoy Huang and his entourage were the first to disembark. All the welcoming personnel crowded around to greet him. Mr. Huang shook hands and thanked them one by one. He then met with reporters from various newspapers in the port and took a car to the Xinya Restaurant on North Sichuan Road to rest. Mr. Huang is in his forties with slightly graying hair, but his spirit is full and there is no sign of travel fatigue. He wore a blue thick woolen overcoat, a black striped suit, and his attitude was amiable when speaking to people.

All Circles Welcome Special Envoy Huang × Photo Taken (Qichang Photography) 108

Huang's Speech

According to Mr. Huang, the process of my entering Tibet has been reported by various newspapers one after another, so there is no need to repeat it. The current situation in Tibet is very good. The people of Tibet have a sincere desire to support the Central Government and also expressed their welcome for the return of the Panchen Lama to Tibet. As for when the Panchen Lama will return to Tibet, I have not heard anything about it. The actions of the British in Tibet are all within the scope of the treaty and there is no special force. The standing army in Tibet is about several thousand people, all conscripted. Since the death of the Dalai Lama, the Tibetan administration has been temporarily represented by the Reting Hutuktu. As for the official successor, he has not yet been produced. It is said that Tibet will send representatives to Beijing to thank the Central Government for its kindness. The candidates have been decided, but the date of departure for Beijing is currently unknown. I am scheduled to go to Beijing today or tomorrow to report everything to the Central Government, he said.

Journey to Tibet

According to Mr. Gao Shifu, who accompanied Special Envoy Huang to Tibet, speaking to the Huadong News Agency, Special Envoy Huang left Beijing on April 26 last year and flew west. Before Special Envoy Huang set off, two batches of entourage had already entered Tibet. The first batch took a ship on March 18 and entered Tibet via India by sea. This included Councilor Jiang and Secretary Wang, etc. The second batch left Beijing on March 28 and went west, led by Deputy Officer Gao and 40 guards, who traveled to Chengdu to wait for Special Envoy Huang. On April 26, after Special Envoy Huang arrived in Chengdu, they set off together for Tibet. On August 28, they finally arrived in Lhasa. They passed through more than twenty large and small mountains along the way, with wind and snow all around, experiencing hardship. However, they were warmly welcomed by the monks and lay people of Tibet along the way, and the Tibetan authorities also protected them with sincerity. The grand reception was unprecedented in decades. Upon arriving in Lhasa, the Tibetan people were particularly happy and encouraged, because they had not seen

If we can get the appropriate guidance from the public opinion, the future is full of hope. Because my vacation has expired, I cannot stay any longer. I originally intended to take the Italian liner to Europe on the 13th, but because of unfinished private affairs, I could not leave. I changed to an American ship and went to Europe via Japan and the United States, so that I can see the situation in Japan and the United States. I am expected to return to my post at the end of March. "

Central Bank Begins to Accept and Exchange Mixed Silver Materials Yesterday 114

Applicants Must First Fill Out an Application Form

After Chemical Examination, Coins Will Be Exchanged Based on Proof

The Central Bank, under the order of the Ministry of Finance, has established a Mixed Silver Materials Exchange Office and began to accept and exchange mixed silver materials yesterday morning. All applicants must first fill out an application form. Mixed silver materials weighing less than 1,500 taels can be exchanged at the bank, and it is stipulated that each yuan shall be converted according to the Silver Standard Coinage Regulations at 23.493448 grams of pure silver, and the minting fee and smelting fee shall be deducted according to law. After the application is made, the bank will specify a date to deliver the materials to the Central Mint for smelting, and the bank will first issue a temporary receipt. After the chemical examination of the quality is completed, the silver standard coins will be exchanged based on the temporary receipt. The application form can be obtained from the Internal Affairs Section of the Business Bureau of the bank. The time is from 10 a.m. to 12 p.m. and 2 p.m. to 3 p.m. every day, and 12 p.m. on Saturdays. Closed on Sundays, it is said that those who went to apply for exchange yesterday included corner coins, silver ingots, and mixed silver blocks. The application was closed at 3 p.m., and about several thousand yuan were exchanged in total.

Ministry of Finance Sends Personnel to Shanghai to Inspect Bank Business 117

Six Legal Items

Nanjing Telephone, since the silver crisis occurred, affecting the entire financial market, some small banks in Shanghai, due to insufficient preparation, have announced liquidation. The Ministry of Finance has the responsibility of supervising the banks and also has the responsibility of representing the society in inspection. In order to prevent such incidents from reoccurring, a ministry order was issued to send Dai Mingli, section chief of the Currency Department, and several others to Shanghai to conduct on-site inspections of various banks. The matters needing attention are: (1) Whether the bank's capital is the same as when originally reported, (2) Whether the reserve of issued banknotes meets the number stipulated by the Ministry of Finance, (3) The total amount of social deposits, (4) Which item the business operation focuses on most, (5) The ratio of loans to deposits, (6) The profit and loss of the business last year. It is said that this inspection is a kind of exercise of supervisory power and has no other meaning. At the same time, because it relates to social trust issues, the procedures do not seek to be pressed and the period depends on the inspection situation. There are no set requirements.

Military Council and Executive Yuan - Issue a Circular to Protect Public Opinion 118

Inspection and Prohibition Must Strictly Abide by Laws and Regulations

The Shanghai Daily Newspaper Association, the Journalists Association, and various newspapers in Tianjin and Beiping, during the Fifth Plenary Session of the Central Committee, separately telegraphed requesting careful handling of news inspection. The plenary session was divided into the Standing Committee of the Central Committee, the Military Affairs Committee, and the Executive Yuan for review. In addition to the Standing Committee of the Central Committee having already resolved the inspection standards and issued a circular for compliance, the Military Affairs Committee and the Executive Yuan have also jointly issued a circular to the provincial and municipal governments, instructing their subordinates to comply with it in its entirety. The original order states: "Case investigation on the occasion of the Fifth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee in December 1934, the various newspapers in Tianjin and Shanghai jointly telegraphed requesting: (1) News inspection should strictly abide by the standards promulgated by the Central Government and be carefully implemented; (2) Disciplinary action against news organizations or reporters should not resort to extraordinary means; (3) For news organizations or reporters who have been suspended, detained, or otherwise punished in the central or local government, as long as they are not backed by force or violence, please reinstate them uniformly. The Central Standing Committee resolved to submit the case to the Committee for review. The investigation and revision of the news inspection standards, the revised measures for news inspection in important cities, and the outline of the measures for news inspection have been successively formulated by the Central Government and circulated for compliance. The procedures for setting up news inspection offices and the standards for news inspection have been detailed in the above-mentioned measures and standards. The newspaper's request regarding (1) news inspection should strictly abide by the standards promulgated by the Central Government and be carefully implemented; (2) disciplinary action against news organizations or reporters should not resort to extraordinary means; are both legitimate. As for (3) news organizations or reporters who have been suspended, detained, or otherwise punished in the central or local government, as long as they are not backed by force or violence, please reinstate them uniformly. The investigation and news inspection, in addition to complying with the provisions of the revised news inspection standards, must also comply with the provisions of Articles 36, 37, 39, 40, and 41 of the Publication Law and Items 2 and 3 of the Examination Standards for Propaganda Products. Note 1 to the revised news inspection standards has already been clearly stipulated. Also, according to Articles 36, 37, 39, 40, and 41 of the Publication Law, if a newspaper violates the Publication Law, its publication may be prohibited, and the publisher, editor, etc., may be sentenced to imprisonment or detention for up to one year. Therefore, it is difficult to uniformly reinstate news organizations or reporters who have been suspended, detained, or otherwise punished in the central or local government, regardless of the circumstances. If those who have been punished believe that the punishment is improper or illegal, they may separately file an appeal or petition, and there is no need to worry about not having a remedy. The original telegram's claim should not be discussed. However, the government has repeatedly issued orders to protect freedom of speech. The inspection and prohibition of various speech organizations by various agencies should be handled in accordance with laws and regulations. In the future, we should encourage even more, and strive to implement the Central Government's policy of supporting public opinion. Freedom of speech is originally freedom within the scope of the law and is not without restrictions. The majority of domestic speech organizations are aware of the overall situation, abide by the law, and love themselves, but there are still some that are unhealthy and immature. Some disclose national military and diplomatic secrets, or knowingly spread rumors in order to achieve the private goal of provoking discord and shaking people's hearts, or harbor grudges and use the position of the newspaper to wantonly damage the reputation of others. Because of this, they violate the law and discipline, or cause retaliation from the injured party. The government should do its best to encourage all fair and excellent newspapers, but it must also enforce the law against those with improper motives who do not know the law. Those who are ignorant of the truth do not investigate the content and add the term "destroying public opinion" to the inspection agencies, hoping to sensationalize the public. In this way, if freedom is spoken of, the result may be that newspapers have freedom, but the people have no protection. The selfishness of a few is fast, and the majority suffers. The loss is small, then the value of public opinion is reduced. If it is large, the interests of the country are damaged, and the malpractices are so numerous, how can they be overcome? For this purpose, all agencies are ordered that they should protect sound public opinion and not abuse their power. For inspection and prohibition matters, they must comply with laws and regulations and not exceed them slightly. On the one hand, they must strictly comply with laws and regulations and not overstep their authority slightly. On the other hand, all speech organizations in various places must also be kindly informed, so that they can restrain themselves and strive to abide by journalistic ethics, and do not abuse the power of newspapers to harm the interests of the country and others, so that the national news industry can be expected to enter the right track, and the effectiveness of public opinion can be promoted, and the foundation of the rule of law can be established. The burden is on this. In addition to separate orders, the order is for compliance, and it is also instructed to forward it to all subordinates for compliance. The Shanghai Daily Newspaper Association has already received the Shanghai Municipal Government's instruction to inform them.

Ministry of Communications Orders China Merchants Bureau to Actively Clear Debts 119

Nanjing Telephone: The Ministry of Communications has ordered the China Merchants Bureau, stating that the debts incurred by the Bureau during the Northern Government era for telecommunications were substantial. The Bureau has been working to clear these debts for over two years, and after several months of negotiation, a resolution has fortunately been reached. Considering that the Bureau's debts related to shipping administration are also significant and resemble the unresolved telecommunications debts, the Bureau should adopt appropriate telecommunications reorganization methods and actively reorganize the debts. The Board should promptly notify the Bureau's creditors to discuss debt clearance and submit a comprehensive debt reorganization plan for approval.

Shipping Administration Bureau Holds Consecutive Shipping Administration Discussion Meetings 129

To Discuss Effective Measures to Promote Shipping Administration

Central News Agency reports that the Shanghai Shipping Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications has established five offices in the provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, including Ningbo, Wuhu, Zhenjiang, Wenzhou, and Fuzhou. Bureau Chief Peng Hu previously went to the respective offices in October and November of last year to understand the local shipping administration and shipping affairs situation and the overall implementation of policies, in order to promote shipping administration. He provided detailed guidance on matters that needed to be rectified and instructed them to improve. For matters related to reforms that need to be reviewed and approved by the Ministry, he selected key recommendations from the inspection report and submitted them to the Ministry for review and handling. As there are many matters requiring reform in various places, it is urgent to gather and discuss effective measures based on the recent situation of each office, and after presenting them for approval, to implement them with full mobilization in order to achieve the purpose of promoting shipping administration. With the approval of the Ministry this month, the heads of the respective offices were convened on the 14th and 15th to hold shipping administration discussion meetings at the Bureau on Sichuan Road. Attendees included Chen Baoyan, the Bureau's secretary, Section Chiefs Chou Lunjie and He Daoyun, Chief Inspector Sun Chengyi, Zhou Jianyin, the director of the Ningbo office, Ye Hongxu, the director of the Wuhu office, Wang Maoqin, the director of the Zhenjiang office, Wu Zhongfei, the director of the Wenzhou office, and Sun Man, the director of the Haizhou office. Section Chief Lou Zhaoding and five others attended as observers. Bureau Chief Peng chaired the meeting. At the beginning of the meeting, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting and the points to be noted in handling affairs. Next, the heads of the respective offices reported on the recent shipping administration situation in various places. Subsequently, proposals were discussed, including 19 cases related to ship management, 4 cases related to limiting shipping routes, 6 cases related to reforming the organization of offices, 2 cases related to supplementing and promoting laws, 2 cases related to crew members, and 9 other cases, totaling 42 cases. After the original proposers explained each case in detail, the members carefully discussed and resolved them one by one. It is reported that the resolutions of each case, once organized, will be reviewed and handled by the Bureau. In addition, special cases will be reported to the Ministry for approval and implementation in order to facilitate the advancement of shipping administration.

The Effect of the Nanjing Road Business Community's Resistance to Abusive Stamp Duty Fines 133

Since the replacement of new stamp duties last winter, the inspection of stamp duties in the concessions has suddenly led to incidents involving unwarranted and innocent cases. In particular, shops on Nanjing Road have been the most affected. For example, employee attendance books at the Huaying Pharmacy and duplicate sales reports at the Taikang Company have been fined 10 yuan per book, totaling a considerable amount. At the time, protests by relevant associations and the Nanjing Road Business Community United Association were ineffective. Subsequently, the Nanjing Road Southern United Association collected fourteen types of books and records that they believed should not require stamp duty and sent them to the Shanghai Inspection Office of the Consolidated Tax Bureau for identification. The Bureau has now replied, stating that five types have been approved for exemption and one type is ambiguous. The Association has issued a notice to its members accordingly. The original text reads: Respected Sirs, Regarding the protest against the excessive inspection of stamp duties in the concessions and the fines imposed on books and records that should not require stamp duty, this Association has collected fourteen types of books and records from several member shops that are believed to be exempt from stamp duty, as listed from A to D in the attached "Standard for Affixing Stamp Duty". Each book is numbered and a description and reason for exemption is provided. These were submitted to the Consolidated Tax Bureau Inspection Office for identification. The Bureau has forwarded the approval from the Tax Administration of the Ministry of Finance to the Association. We are now forwarding the attached sheet listing the standard for determining whether stamp duty should be affixed as specified in the original approval document for your reference. However, for clarity, the types that can be exempted are listed below: (1) Sign-in Book, (2) Book Cover of Invoice Stubs, (3) Attendance Record (this term is not common; it refers to a sign-in book with a form recording employee duty shifts), (4) Leave of Absence Book, (5) Payment Certificate (specifically for internal use by shops), (6) Material Issuance Record (this applies to clothing stores with custom-made clothing; since there are items such as "custom order", the approval requires stamp duty to be affixed according to regulations to prevent exploitation; if it is purely for internal material issuance, it can naturally be exempted). Furthermore, according to the official letter, the attached sheet has been instructed to be notified to the concession inspection offices for their information. If, in the future, the above-mentioned books and records that are exempt from stamp duty are inspected or detained, please politely refuse to present them based on this certificate. Sincerely, Shanghai Special First District Citizen First District Branch Nanjing Road Business Community United Association, issued February 15, 24th year of the Republic, with one attached sheet.

Standard for Affixing Stamp Duty (Approved by the Shanghai Consolidated Tax Inspection Office) A. Pharmacy Department, Sign-in Book: Determined to be unrelated, exempt from stamp duty. B. Accounting Department, Sign-in Book: Same as above. C. Invoice Stub Matching Book in the Receipting Department: Belongs to a type of business account, determined to be related to business, stamp duty should be affixed. D. Invoice Book: Since the invoice has already had stamp duty affixed, the book cover is exempt. E. Sample Mailing Book: Belongs to a type of business ledger, determined to be related to business, stamp duty should be affixed. F. Attendance Record: Determined to be unrelated to business, exempt from stamp duty. G. Goods Inspection Book: Belongs to a type of business ledger, determined to be related to business, stamp duty should be affixed. H. Ring and Line Ring Book: Determined to be the same in nature as the previous goods inspection book, stamp duty should be affixed. I. Leave of Absence Book: Determined to be unrelated to business, exempt from stamp duty. J. Payment Certificate: Should be exempt if it is definitely for internal use. K. Clothing Cutting Book: Belongs to a type of business ledger, determined to be related to business, stamp duty should be affixed. L. Custom Clothing Order Form: Determined to be the same in nature as a receipt for goods purchased on pre-order, stamp duty should be affixed to each form. M. Material Issuance Record: If this type of document is specifically for material issuance, then the custom clothing order form opened when the customer orders clothing must have the words "Amount Paid" and "Deposit Received". Why must this type of document also specify the amount of money? Fundamentally, it belongs to a type of custom clothing order form. In reality, it is not for internal material issuance. It should still follow the example of documents for pre-ordered goods and have stamp duty affixed to prevent exploitation. N. Daily Report Book: Resembles a running ledger, related to business, stamp duty should be affixed according to the example of loose-leaf ledgers.

Zhabei Civilian Education and Rehabilitation Center's First Step of Implementation Plan Successful 135

Diligently and Earnestly Engaging in the Work

Self-Sufficiency and Self-Support Worthy of Admiration

Wang Guan Yi Resigns as Director

After the January 28 Incident, the Shanghai Municipal Local Maintenance Association, concerned about the concentration of vagrants in Zhabei as a hidden danger to the area, allocated 100,000 yuan from relief funds as a foundation. When the Shanghai Municipal Local Coordination Association was established, it continued to manage the center, first expanding new houses on the old site of the Liuying Road Vocational Training Center in Zhabei. It was completed in the spring of the 22nd year of the Republic and transferred more than 100 civilians from places such as the South Shanghai Chronic Illness Center for education and rehabilitation, with equal emphasis on work and training. Later, due to various reasons, the management was formally entrusted to the China Children's Welfare Association on August 1st of the 23rd year of the Republic, with a contract period of two years. The Association's Secretary-General Xu Jianping sought approval from Chairman Kong Xiangxi to select and dispatch Wang Guan Yi to take over and organize the center in advance. Subsequently, the Association's Executive Committee formally appointed Wang Guan Yi as Director. Following Chairman Kong's instructions, Wang Guan Yi focused on scientific management and production development to achieve the goal of self-sufficiency and self-support. Director Wang, with a spirit of practical experimentation and hard work, worked to complete this mission, and sought guidance from the directors of the Local Coordination Association, such as Du Yuesheng, Qian Xinzhi, Wang Binyan, Zhang Xiaoliang, Huang Renzhi, Jiang Wenyu, and Hu Yunqiu, as well as support from people in the community, the center's Management Committee members Ding Shujing, Lin Kanghou, and Li Tingan, and assistance from the Association's Secretary-General Xu and colleagues. As a result, the first step of the center's self-sufficiency and self-support implementation plan was successful. To clarify the facts and encourage observation, the main points are explored below: (1) Emerging industries and expansion of existing industrial and agricultural sectors, (1) Ping An Chicken Farm, using the center's strip of land, selecting residents, and managing it with scientific methods and economic management, (2) China Stone Company, the only domestic natural stone company in China, with the enthusiastic support of the company, has reportedly transferred a portion of its simple work to the center, and no fewer than 20 residents are learning this craft, (2) Paper Box Factory, in addition to manufacturing mosquito coil boxes for the China Chemical Industry Society, has also received approval from Mr. Hou of Fuxin Tobacco Company to manufacture all the paper boxes for the factory's Holmes cigarettes, so the factory's income has also increased accordingly, (4) Laundry Department, originally established to wash the clothes of the center's staff and workers, is now also washing clothes for the Guanzhen Restaurant on Sichuan Road and the Association's Children's Welfare Clinic on Baoshan Road, so it has improved its washing techniques and increased its income, (5) Farm Animal Husbandry, comprehensively reformed, vegetable production, in addition to supplying the center, is also sold to the Buddhist Children's Welfare Home, the Association's Tangshan Road Education and Rehabilitation Center, and nearby restaurants, etc., with considerable monthly income, animal husbandry, in addition to the previously raised pigs and sheep, which are sold during the lunar New Year, now also includes goats, pigs, etc., (2) Economic situation, the center's economic sources, in addition to the local Coordination Association's monthly allocation of 600 yuan from the foundation's interest, the Association's monthly provision of 400 yuan in subsidies (a six-month trial period is full, subsidies stop after the period). The center's director, with the importance of the mission of self-sufficiency and self-support, and with the determination to achieve nothing less than success, immediately reduced expenditures from one side and increased revenue from the other side, such as the above-mentioned improvement of the industrial and agricultural sectors, which increased production. In the first month, expenses were reduced by more than one-third compared to the past. Up to now (a total of six months), the center's operating expenses, in addition to the local Coordination Association's allocation of foundation interest and designated donations, the Association's monthly subsidy has been used for only a few dozen yuan. Therefore, the first step of the center's plan has indeed been successful, and future progress will be even more limitless. (3) Education and rehabilitation methods (emphasis on conversion) (1) Physical training, focusing on military training and recreational activities, so that each resident has balanced health development and can undertake various daily tasks, (2) Use of hands and feet, enriching the original factories and farms, and improving them so that each resident's hands and feet learn considerable skills and create self-reliant talents, (3) Development of the brain, focusing on the input of knowledge, teaching the characters needed for daily life, simple science, and common civic knowledge, (4) Broadening of knowledge, so that the residents' sight, hearing, and feeling, as much as possible, go to see and hear, and make contact in person. Therefore, the center focuses on travel, visits, autonomous gatherings, film education, etc., such as visiting American warships, visiting the Municipal Government, visiting exhibitions, and admiring famous gardens, all to reduce the narrow-minded attitude of being surprised by the unfamiliar and to promote their bright and upright thinking, (5) Correction of bad habits, in addition to daily education, the formation of public and private morality is carefully arranged in the environment, personal contact, and joint discipline, with the aim of purifying their inferior nature invisibly. The center's ability to achieve self-sufficiency in a short period of time, without relying on assistance, is a model for children's welfare institutions across the country. At the same time, the center has abundant development potential in its environment. If it continues to work hard in this way, it will not be difficult to use the unlimited environment to complete a greater mission.

It has also been learned that Director Wang, due to the numerous duties within the association, is unable to take care of everything, and that all matters within the center are on track, with economic independence having been achieved, and that the time is right for him to resign and hand over his position to a more capable person. He has submitted his resignation, so the center's Management Committee has separately sought out talent and submitted it to the Executive Committee for appointment and replacement.

The Shanghai Lawyers Association yesterday sent a notice to all members of the Legal Aid Society for the Poor, stating that, in response to a notification from the Shanghai First Special District District Court, although there are many designated defense lawyers who appear in court on the designated date to provide defense, it is not uncommon for them to be absent due to unforeseen circumstances. Social Affairs Bureau, Due to the Glut of Foreign Rice, Decides to Order Long-Term Rice from Suifenhe and Other Locations 139

Approved by Order of the Municipal Government

Last year, Jiangxi and Zhejiang provinces experienced drought, and agricultural yields were sharply reduced. To regulate the people's food supply, the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau petitioned the municipal government to purchase long-term foreign rice. At the same time, financial institutions and rice merchants also ordered foreign rice from Saigon, Rangoon, and other locations, to be shipped to China in installments. Now, the bureau believes that the total amount of foreign rice registered for import has reached 6,235,000 bags, equivalent to 623,500 tons, and the market is already glutted with foreign rice. Therefore, there is no need to order more long-term foreign rice. It has specially requested the municipal government to approve a postponement, which has been approved by order.

Wen Zong'e, Connected to Zunde Lane Opium Manufacturing Organization, Further Apprehended 142

Wen Previously Illegally Detained by the Japanese

Also Suspected of Aiding Drug Manufacturing

Detectives stationed by the Lao Zha Police Department at the residence of Chen Zongchang, the main criminal of the Zunde Lane opium den at 21 Xiejiao Road, apprehended Yue native Wen Zong'e at approximately 11:00 AM the day before yesterday and brought him back to the police station. Wen stated that he resides at No. 8 Huanlong Lane, Longhuan Lane, is a graduate of Meiji University in Japan, and is currently a staff member of the Seventh District of the Consolidated Tax Bureau. He claimed that his visit to Chen's residence was because Chen had privately imported Japanese-made cigarette paper and evaded taxes, so he was investigating. The detectives accompanied him to the Consolidated Tax Bureau for investigation, where a Mr. Wang, a senior official, identified him as an employee of the bureau but stated that he had not been dispatched to Chen's residence for investigation. The detectives, believing that Wen's statement was untrue, took him back to the police station. Wen then claimed that in addition to his position at the Consolidated Tax Bureau, he also held a position at the Nichijitsu Hibi (transliteration) Foreign Firm and was there on behalf of the foreign firm to collect payment for cigarette paper from Chen Zonglian. After investigation by the detectives, it was learned that Chen indeed had a debt dispute with the foreign firm. Recently, Chen was illegally detained by the Japanese in a certain area of Hongkou, and Wen threatened Chen with a gun at the time, resulting in his arrest. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Special District Court's Criminal Division One. Police attorney Wang Yaotang explained the situation and stated that in addition to being suspected of aiding in the manufacture of heroin, the defendant was also guilty of obstructing freedom and requested permission to detain him for joint trial with Chen Zongchang, Tang Jiejun, and others. Judge Feng Bozhang briefly questioned him and ordered him detained pending further investigation.
