Tidbits 203

— (Yan Hao)

Before the age of twenty, people are inexperienced; after the age of fifty, energy gradually declines. The thirty years in between, however, are carelessly wasted! When exactly do people live and work?

The woodpecker is indeed a strange bird, specializing in eating woodworms. I really don't know if it exists for the sake of woodworms, or seeks woodworms for the sake of existence?

In the morning, I heard the rattling sound of an airplane. I thought that people were soaring into the sky, while I was still lying in bed, so I couldn't help but get up.

On West Lake, pavilions, tombs, terraces, and pagodas are everywhere. The landscape does not need such things to embellish it, but such things must embellish the landscape!

Elementary School Students 204

— Wei Jing

As soon as the bell rings, dozens of elementary school students pour out of each classroom. - This is the scene of dismissal at an elementary school.

Thus, a large open space is filled with the future masters of China. Although some are playing with large and small balls, most of them are running around, chasing and fighting with all their might, verbally abusing the ancestors of the chased for seventeen or eighteen generations.

Clusters of them are playing "Three Iron Roosters" learned from their fathers taking them to the theater, or "Cloud Comes, Fog Goes, Win or Lose" tricks obtained from novels rented from door-panel book stalls. Other clusters are playing marbles on the ground, rolling coins, desperately trying to lead the money in other people's pockets into their own.

These games are not for girls. The extracurricular work of girls in small cheongsams or long coats and short skirts is always to protect their younger brothers and sisters, or to talk with their female classmates about how to cut their hair, what color to make their scarves, or what Mr. So-and-so's long gown is like, and how Mr. So-and-so speaks. But in elementary schools, girls are as easily bullied by boys as women are in ordinary society. It is a common and uneventful thing for a girl to be standing nicely and to be pinched, groped, or hit by a boy.

At the school gate, there are crowded vendors. "Five-spice peanuts," "Hong Kong beef," "Preserved tangerine peel," "Lard and fruit sesame candy," etc., are all available. There is also "One copper to win a prize," "Thirty-six doors, every door has a prize." There are also "Three copper coins for a pencil, twenty cents for a fountain pen." There are also, and there are endless forms and styles, and every stall is crowded with elementary school students.

The bell rings again, and the elementary school students flock into the classrooms, flocking into the classrooms to receive education to become the future masters of China.

Charming Suzhou 205

— Shijiu

Suzhou is so charming. It is like a beauty, intoxicated in a pink dream, sometimes giggling, sometimes slightly frowning, enough to make people feel short of breath when they see it.

Radio broadcasts are noisy all day long. If you walk through Guanqian Street, you can hear all kinds of tunes you have never heard before. No, even if you walk through the streets and alleys, you can see tall antennas crisscrossing. This proves that wireless radios have become a blessing for every household in Suzhou.

Since the advent of wireless radio, Suzhou has added many performing artists, who were very popular for a while. Today, Qian Mansion in Taohuawu orders "Crying Seven Seven": tomorrow, Li in Lianxifang orders "Afraid of Wife," Huang in Daru Lane orders "Little Orphan Widow": the day after tomorrow, a store on Lindun Road orders "Comic Daochang," Zhao in Gushixiang orders "Catching Zhang Sanlang Alive." They—the performing artists—are really too busy. According to their reports, they are very honored to receive many letters from all walks of life requesting songs. But in one day, some order "Crying Seven Seven," some order "Afraid of Wife," and some order... It is really like the public wants wontons and the mother-in-law wants noodles, which makes them really embarrassed. Because time is limited and they only have one mouth, the words "Junior," "Apologies," etc., have become their opening remarks before broadcasting.

Just in terms of hearing, Suzhou is charming enough. In terms of sight, there is no need to talk about daytime. Once it gets dark, if you stroll through Guanqian Street, you will be dazzled. The towering bank buildings and the red and green New Year lanterns, although not as grand as Shanghai's Avenue Joffre, are enough to be charming.

Suzhou is charming, and Suzhou is intoxicated in a pink dream.

"Rearmament" "If the sword is lost, peace is also lost." Soldiers eventually become white bones!

— Yin Juan

Skating 206

— Beiping Guest

Although the New World had a skating game department eight or nine years ago, those skating games were just skating on the floor with wheeled skates, which is very different from our Beiping skating;

Beiping's ice rinks can be divided into two types; one is natural, which is those lakes or small rivers that freeze thick in early December of the lunar calendar, becoming natural ice rinks. The other is artificial, which is because the weather in the north is too cold, so a lot of water is poured in the courtyard overnight, and it will become an artificial ice rink tomorrow. The most famous natural ice rinks in Beiping are those of Yanjing University, and the three places of Nanhai and Beihai. The artificial ones are the ice rinks of Xiehe Hospital and Tsinghua University.

Skating shoes are not like the four-wheeled skates we see in Shanghai; they are a pair of long boots made of camel down, with a thin blade about two inches wide nailed to the bottom of the shoe. Therefore, for beginners, not to mention skating with this kind of skates, it is not easy to stand on the ice with a balanced body!

There are many skating games, in addition to ice racing, ice hockey, and writing patterns with skates, the best looking are the ice solo dance and duet dance. The graceful dance on the ice is much more beautiful than the dance partners on the smooth floor of any dance hall!

World Rare News

The Standard of Beauty 207

— Bing Yu

A professor of hygiene at the Technology Institute in Mesa, USA, recently published a method for judging beauty, which is to calculate the points of each part of the body. Only those who can get 100 points can be considered completely beautiful. His scoring method is very precise. That is: (1) Set the weight according to age and height as 20 points. (2) Hair has a shiny color when it is not oiled, set as 5 points. (3) Eyes are clean and clear, but those with yellow whites are still inferior, only clear and shiny eyes are 5 points. (4) The shape of the mouth shows happiness everywhere, set as 5 points, but those that droop when breathing are still inferior. (5) Teeth are very tight when chewing, set as 5 points. (6) The skin is bright and smooth, the texture is fine, and the cheeks and lips have natural color, set as 10 points. (7) The nails are clean, smooth, beautiful, and the entry and exit length are very perfect, set as 5 points. (8) The foot shape has natural beauty, and the line from the heel to the big toe is straight and not crooked, set as 10 points. (9) In terms of posture, the shoulders are balanced from left to right, the wrists are relaxed, the abdominal line is beautiful, and the two feet are parallel and slightly apart, set as 5 points. The shape of sitting is beautiful, set as 2 points. The ability to coordinate movement when walking, set as 2 points. Able to hear ordinary conversations from sixteen feet away, and have healthy hearing, set as 5 points. Two arms straight and have reading vision, set as 5 points. (10) In terms of health, the mind and body are refreshed, have self-control and enthusiasm, etc., set as 10 points. (11) The clothing can suit the personality and the time and place of the center, set as 5 points. According to this scoring method, among the female students of large, medium, and small schools, almost none meet the above 11 points, and those who get 96 points are only one person. This is based on the evaluations of various parties in Mesa, and it can be seen that it is really rare to be able to fully meet the above conditions.

Hairiweisima Ya and other beauty experts from Shenglin recently evaluated the standard of women's beauty from the three points of harmony, balance, and beauty. Among them, Ms. Xi Luoweiya Xituoni was praised by all the professional beauticians and considered the only and unique beauty. Ms. Xituoni is a native of Southern California. She was selected as the "Standard of Beauty" by the Southern California Beautician Association. The appearance of this lady, according to the structure of geometry, has almost no faults. That is: (1) The length of the face is three times that of the nose. (2) The space between the eyes and the middle of the eyes has the position of one eye. (3) The width of the upper lip is not bad at all. (4) The shoulder hair extension line harmonized from left to right converges at a point on the nose. (5) The gap between the lower face and the upper face is equal to the gap between the upper face and the eyebrows. (6) The eye is closest to the nose, separated from the middle of the upper part of the eye, without any difference. (7) The width of the cheek is exactly twice as large as the nose. After this standard beauty was published, women in Southern California went to beauty salons to be identified, but none were as neat as Ms. Xituoni.

Small West Heaven 208

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Ninth Episode: Poor Flattery Leads to Scolding; Unable to Return, He Follows the Guest's Exaggerations

He sighed and said, "You, Madam, are thinking too much. With feet as small as yours, you can barely walk, how can you come out to work?" Madam Hu was about to sit down on the chair, but upon hearing this, she immediately supported herself on the table and stood up, saying, "Old Master Zhang, you haven't been to Gansu, you don't know. Women there, at home, wash clothes and cook, and outside, they can plant and harvest grain in the fields." Jie Fu looked at her, seeing her steadying herself on the table, still swaying slightly, and shook his head with a smile, saying, "No matter what, I cannot believe what you say. Even now, you can barely stand here, how can you work?" Madam Hu said, "What you say is true. However, in Gansu, we don't stand to work, we kneel to work." Hearing this, Jie Fu couldn't help but be surprised and looked at her, saying, "What? Kneel to work?" Jie Fu, hearing this, couldn't help but be surprised and looked at her, saying, "What? Kneel to work? At home, you can kneel to work, but when you go out the gate, to the fields, do you still kneel to work?" Madam Hu said, "Why not? As soon as we get there, we kneel down. We are not like the women of Xi'an, who can stand." As she spoke, her body swayed twice more. Jie Fu quickly waved his hand at her and said, "Terrible, terrible, just sit down, we'll talk slowly." Madam Hu, in fact, couldn't afford to be polite and sat down. Jie Fu moved the rattan-wrapped teapot on the table in front of her and said, "I won't stand on ceremony with you, there are teacups on the table, pour yourselves a drink. It's chilling." Madam Hu touched the lid of the rattan wrapping and then withdrew her hand. Yueying, standing on the side, said, "Drink it, it's nothing to drink two cups of tea from this old master." Hearing this, Madam Hu boldly drank two cups of tea. It was much warmer inside the house than outside. It was already late spring, and without the wind blowing, it wasn't too cold, so after two cups of warm tea, her spirits improved a lot. While she was drinking tea, Jie Fu couldn't help but look at Yueying. (134)

Record of Royal Fragrance, Misty and Floating 209

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Didn't I already say above that whenever the Empress Dowager had any unpleasant feelings, everyone in the palace would become worried? Therefore, we always tried our best to make her happy, especially in these gloomy ancient Shengjing palaces. If we didn't find some suitable spiritual adjustments, we would truly become lifeless! Therefore, when I thought that today was the fifteenth of the month, and according to custom, opera should be performed, I felt extremely happy in my heart.

"Old Buddha!" Although I didn't see her face as very gentle this morning, in order to remove this heavy cloud of sorrow, I boldly said to her, "Today is the fifteenth of the month again! Shouldn't we have an opera performance? In my humble opinion, letting the ancestors here also see our lively entertainment, so that they know that the world is still as prosperous and peaceful as before, wouldn't that be a very good way to show filial piety? Furthermore, since we no longer have any good places to go out and play here, just sitting around is too boring! Watching opera is the best pastime."

The Empress Dowager, upon hearing my words, actually revealed a trace of a smile and nodded her head slightly.

"That's right! Your idea is indeed good! Just do as you say!" She approved my suggestion without any hesitation.

"In that case, please instruct, Old Buddha, which operas should be performed today?" My risky attempt having succeeded, I became bolder and quickly urged her to select the plays.

"I have no preconceived notions, just pick one or two operas that you like to listen to!" Her smile gradually revealed itself. (245)

Shen Bao Wireless Weekly

Radio Reception Record Form 210

— Li Yuanqing

—Meaning of Approved Audio Signal Symbols—

After a radio receives an incoming broadcast, its readings must be recorded to avoid the trouble of re-searching in the future, as everyone knows.

Simply recording the readings has no other value besides providing entertainment convenience. If one wants to meet practical needs and scientific reference, the scope of the records must be researched and expanded.

Radio reception is often better in cold weather than in hot weather, and better at night than during the day, so the first step is to record the date and time.

Secondly, the weather conditions, such as overcast skies, the presence of the moon, as well as temperature and air pressure, also affect the transmission and reception of radio waves, so recording the weather is also very important.

If the radio's location is frequently changed, the length, height, and direction of the antenna, as well as the location, must also be noted.

When receiving distant broadcasts, the signal strength fluctuates. This phenomenon is called fading in radio science. The reasons for this have been described in my article "Fading in Radios" in issue 77 of this publication. It varies at any time, any moment, and any place, so the state of fading must also be recorded.

The presence or absence of atmospheric electricity or other interference must also be noted.

The most difficult thing to record is the quality of the audio. The recording of this item has always been done according to individual preferences, with no regulations. Such a lack of regulation is, of course, not in line with scientific principles. In order to remedy this deficiency, the radio industry has defined the following two standard audio signal symbols:

(1) Volume Symbol: Usually represented by R, with nine levels of strength:

R1 Extremely weak R6 Fairly strong

R2 Very weak R7 Strong

R3 Weak R8 Very strong

R4 Fairly weak R9 Extremely strong

R5 Acceptable

(2) Quality Symbol: Broadcasts from distant locations are often difficult to understand clearly. Sometimes, even if they are very loud, they are still difficult to distinguish due to various interferences. Therefore, a quality symbol is also specified, usually represented by Q.

Q1 Unintelligible

Q2 Only one or two words are intelligible

Q3 Difficult to distinguish

Q4 Easy to distinguish

Q5 Every word is very clear

For example, if the audio signal symbols are R8 and Q5, it means that the volume of a certain station is very loud and the audio quality is extremely clear.

In addition, the location, call sign, and frequency or wavelength of the station are all well-known to the general public and are detailed in the attached table, so they will not be elaborated on in this article.

From Radio Calibration Curves to Experimental Measurement Methods for Coil Inductance 211

— Wang Shengshi

Anyone who has a radio should draw their own calibration curve. This curve is very useful; it not only tells you the location of each station but also helps you find distant stations.

What is a calibration curve? I think most readers already know, but since it will be used below, it may be worthwhile to explain it simply again. Every radio has a tuning circuit consisting of a coil and a variable capacitor. The dial of this capacitor is usually divided into one hundred divisions. The dial of this capacitor is usually divided into one hundred divisions. Turning this capacitor allows you to receive stations of different frequencies.

Now, take a piece of graph paper, with one hundred small divisions horizontally representing the dial readings and the vertical axis representing the station's kilocycle frequency, ranging from 500 to 1500 (as shown in Figure 2). Then, pay attention to the stations you hear. For example, if you hear the Central Broadcasting Station at 90 degrees, mark a point at 90 on the horizontal axis and write down the words "Central." The Central Broadcasting Station is at 660 kilocycles, so go up from this point and mark a point at 660. Use the same method to record the other stations one by one. Stations in Shanghai often report their call signs, so this step can be completed soon. Then, connect the many points with a curve plate to get a curve or a straight line, depending on the type of capacitor. I use the Ame 3121, so the curve drawn is as shown in the figure. Its greatest use is twofold:

(1) The location of a station with a known frequency can be determined from the curve. For example, the Fuzhou Broadcasting Station is located between the Eastern and Central-Western stations and is usually inaudible (when using a regenerative DC three-tube radio in Kunshan), but because it is 1030 kilocycles, it is known from the curve that it must be at 29 degrees. On the night of the 28th, when both the Eastern and Central-Western stations were off the air, turning the dial to 29 degrees clearly heard the report in the loudspeaker.

(2) The frequency of any station heard can be determined from the curve. My radio has heard eight Japanese stations, none of whose call signs I have heard, but a check of the curve can reveal their station names. For example, there is a Japanese station at 87 degrees next to the Central Broadcasting Station. From the curve, it is known that it must be 670 kilocycles, which is the Taipei Broadcasting Station.

This curve also has another use, which is that it can be used to find the inductance L of the coil. We know that the station's reading is closely related to the inductance L and the capacitance C, expressed by the formula:

where F is the station's frequency, L is the inductance (Henry), and C is the capacitance (Farad).

The maximum capacitance of ordinary capacitors C is known. For example, the Ame 3121 is 0.0003 microfarads. This value is the capacitance when the dial is turned to 100 degrees. What frequency does this point correspond to? If there is a station exactly at 100 degrees, that's the best. If not, the curve can be extended smoothly to 100 degrees to see what the frequency is at that point. Because the curve is already close to a straight line at low frequencies, there is no difficulty in extending it. In the case of my radio, the frequency is 630 kilocycles when the dial is turned to 100 degrees, which is F. Substituting the values of F and C into the formula, we get:

The value of L is found to be 0.00021 Henry, which is the inductance of the coil L.

When the dial of the capacitor is turned to zero degrees, the capacitance is not zero. From the calibration curve, we know that the frequency at this point is 1500 kilocycles. Substituting this into the formula again:

The value of C is found to be 0.00006 microfarads. Therefore, it is known that the capacitance of the Ame 3121 capacitor when the fixed and moving plates are completely separated is 0.00006 microfarads.

This method can be applied to the tuning circuit of any broadcast radio. However, the capacitance of variable capacitors made by manufacturers is not very accurate, so the results obtained will naturally have some errors.

Selection of Shortwave Wavelengths 212

— Jian

The propagation state of shortwaves varies with wavelength (frequency), and there are cases where communication is completely impossible due to seasonal and nighttime conditions. Therefore, one should pay attention to selecting a certain wavelength (frequency) in a certain season or at a certain time. Regarding the appropriate selection in the amateur wavelength band (frequency band), it can be roughly divided into the following categories:

(1) The 7,000 KC band and the 14,000 KC band are the most widely used, and nighttime long-distance experiments all utilize them, especially the 14,000 KC band is most suitable for daytime long-distance communication.

(2) The bands that are commonly used at night are 1,750 KC, 8,500 KC, 7,000 KC, and 14,000 KC. Among these, the 7,000 KC band is the most popular.

(3) For long-distance communication during the daytime in summer, the most suitable frequency bands are 28,000 KC and 14,000 KC. The 1,750 KC frequency band is best suited for communication within two to three hundred miles, as it is easier to oscillate and is suitable for use by beginners.

Underwater Radio 213

— Li Jian

According to a scientific news report in the Soviet newspaper Pravda, the "Whale Ship" engineering unit, which is salvaging a sunken ship on the bottom of the Black Sea, has repeatedly tried underwater radio broadcasting over the years of salvage work, but without good results. However, they continued their research without slackening, and finally, at the end of December last year, they broadcast the message of victory from the seabed of the Black Sea using underwater radio. According to the person in charge of salvaging the sunken ship, they specially designed a waterproof and lightweight broadcasting and receiving set, attached to the back of a waterproof suit, which does not add much weight and is very functional, and can also broadcast and receive at any time and any place, so that they can establish extremely close communication with the shore.

When the first underwater radio was used for the launching ceremony, Maxim Mens (the commander-in-chief of salvaging the sunken ship) said: In his life of salvaging sunken ships, he had never seen such a difficult and arduous task as salvaging the "Whale Ship." Now, after a long period of struggle, we have invented this underwater radio, and it will be much easier to use it to direct all the work of salvaging the "Whale Ship." Now we are not only completely confident that the sunken "Whale Ship" can be completely salvaged, but also that our work in salvaging sunken ships can be called the best in the world. After he finished speaking, he ordered the salvage divers to broadcast the lyrics underwater: "We will conquer everything; we have conquered it. We will overcome everything; we have overcome it. Forward! Forward! The victory of science belongs to us..." All the listeners who heard this broadcast shouted "Long live!" and dispersed.

The major Moscow radio materials manufacturing plants are now actively rushing to produce the special materials needed for underwater radio, and are opening short-term crash courses to train this type of skilled personnel, in order to expand and improve all future salvage work.

Small Experience

Method for Restoring Demagnetized Earpieces 214

— Zhou Wenwei

Regarding this issue, I have seen many great works. Some use natural magnets to rub back and forth on the demagnetized magnetic poles to restore them. Some use electromagnets, with current flowing, to connect to the demagnetized magnetic poles to restore them. Both methods are good and can be used. However, after the author's experimentation, I feel that there are three drawbacks: (1) not easy to magnetize, (2) the magnetic force is not strong after magnetization, (3) very easy to lose magnetism after magnetization. I believe that readers who have tried it will feel the same way! Now I will publish the new method I discovered during the holidays for restoring magnetic force (1. inexpensive, 2. simple method, 3. everyone can do it, 4. strong magnetic force, 5. not easy to lose), for the reference of fellow enthusiasts.

Restoration method: Take the black wire of the demagnetized earpiece and connect it to the ground wire (the person experimenting must stand on a stool to isolate the human body from the earth's atmosphere to avoid the danger of electric shock). Then, touch the red wire to the live wire of the electric light, and immediately remove it (if the time is too long, the thin wire inside the earpiece will be burned). The demagnetized earpiece will then be restored, just like new. (When connecting to the live wire of the electric light, if no spark is found, it is connected incorrectly and should be reversed). The author can guarantee that this method will not fail.

Free Talk

Contradictions on the Knowledge Line 215

— He Sheng

The school opening date for the spring semester has long passed by more than ten days. However, Shanghai newspapers are still crowded with enrollment advertisements for primary and secondary schools, and this is the third or even fourth time they are recruiting. This tells us that there are many schools and teachers in Shanghai, but there is a lack of students. Why is this happening? The answer is because of the economic recession! The recession has made it impossible for most people to afford school fees.

However, the newspapers also reported that many primary schools in the Jiangzhe interior are owed salaries, with some owing eight months and others owing four or five months. The "sacred and noble" primary school teachers have nothing left but their stomachs, so they have all gone on strike. A certain county in Zhejiang originally had six primary schools. Since last winter, there have been strikes and suspensions, and not a single day has there been two schools in session at the same time. Many primary school students have no choice but to be idle. Isn't this the opposite of Shanghai, where there are schools and teachers but a lack of students? However, this is also because of the economic recession! Because the recession has affected several "dedicated funds" for the source of education funding.

The widespread recession has also affected bookstores. It is said that most of the bookstores in Shanghai lack cash. However, judging from the accounts, almost every one has a surplus. The surplus is in accounts receivable. Since they are still open, new books must be published; however, if the new books don't sell, they can only be piled up high in the press. If they do sell, what they get is also an account. To publish or not to publish? This is another contradiction.

However, at the same time, the readers (although this is only a very small circle) are crying out that there is nothing to read! Bookstore owners are trying to find new books that can have a wide readership, but the vast majority of readers often feel that there is nothing to read. This contradiction is also ridiculously severe.

Last year was the year of magazines. The excitement was unprecedented. However, according to surveys, the sales of various magazines have only fallen. Being able to maintain the original state without falling is considered excellent. This fact clearly points out that the increase in magazines is not directly proportional to the increase in readers. Then is it because the number of authors has increased? It is said that this is not entirely true either. The editors of magazines will tell you how few submissions are usable and how difficult it is to solicit articles. Isn't this another contradiction?

Contradictions on the knowledge line have never been as numerous and severe as they are now! If one puts in the effort to collect materials, this contradictory account can be said to be endless. If these contradictions cannot be resolved, any plan for reviving Chinese culture will be just an unfunded check. And these contradictions have a common root cause, which is the social recession and chaos!

What I Saw in Front of the Java Customs 216

— Feier

Having just crossed the sturdy plank bridge in front of the customs office onto the Banjir coast, I was blocked by a large crowd.

Malay youths and children were solemnly surrounding the open space in front of the customs office, while Chinese coolies and shop assistants were watching the main characters acting in the square with the attitude of onlookers, as if they were watching a play – the men of the Empire.

Pushing my way through the crowd, I saw several "masters of Asia" wearing wooden clogs and kimonos, pointing at the customs office and cursing angrily, with an unusually imposing and impassioned attitude.

"You, what small customs officer, dare to mess with us?" one cursed. The Malay language was enunciated very clearly, just like the English commonly used by the men of the Empire. However, because of anger, the syllables were bitten even more firmly, turning the unstressed syllables into sturdy copper and iron.

Another, grasping his hand, approached the entrance of the Shanghai Customs Office, and his cursing resounded throughout the entire Banjir coast:

"If you dare, come out in front of the customs office for a duel! We Japanese won't put a small Javanese customs officer in our eyes."

Another middle-aged man in his forties or fifties, seemed somewhat more amiable, but he stood in the middle of the square with his hands clasped, murmuring:

"See how they reckon with us. See if he dares to bully us!"

A-Xing stood on a pair of wooden boxes and asked a Malay man next to him:

"What's going on?"

The small, thin Malay man said in a gloomy, low voice (his voice was unusually low, as if he was afraid of being heard by the furious people):

"Who knows. Maybe it's about taxes. It is said that the Java customs officer levied too high a tax on a Japanese man's goods, and they started arguing in the customs office. So they gathered all five fellow countrymen in the city, leaving their wives and children to watch the store, and all came here to demonstrate."

A-Yu laughed loudly and said:

"You 'slaves of a fallen nation' deserve to be trampled on by wooden clogs."

These words stung the Malay youth somewhat. That one suddenly said excitedly:

"Even you 'Chinamen' are not necessarily not bullied by the Japanese, are you? We, we have the newly rising Turkey."

"No, we 'Chinese,' we dare to fight the Japanese."

Captain-Mr. felt a little annoyed when he heard these words. He frowned and urged us to leave quickly. On the one hand, he was already very tired; on the other hand, perhaps he felt that these arguments were a bit inappropriate?

Although I didn't see an end to the incident in front of the customs office, A-Xing dragged me away out of anger.

On the way, A-Yu still said angrily:

"Damn it, it's really a chaotic world - last year, a Japanese fishing boat rushed into the Lu River Customs Office in the middle of the night and caused it to sink. Our Chinese fishermen helped to salvage it. Wait for the customs office to come and ask afterwards, you know what they said?"

"We encountered wind at sea. We took refuge here. Your customs office doesn't even turn on the lights at night, how can we know where the customs office is hidden - now that the ship has sunk, you should also bear some responsibility."

"Damn it, encountered wind? If our Chinese ships barge in without declaring in the middle of the night, the ships won't be detained, but they'll have to pay a fine. And them, it is said that after the ships are repaired, the government gives them a subsidy."

"Damn it, thinking of the humiliating term 'Chinaman' really makes one angry!"

Captain-Mr. and I walked silently, not speaking for a while. After some consideration, Captain-Mr. finally came to the following conclusion:

"It's all because we are too disunited. Look at them, as soon as a small incident occurs, all five of them come out in full force."

"Are we not united? Why are we not united?" A-Xing asked back, a rational question suppressing his fiery emotions.

"Why should we be united?" I wanted to use K to refute, but I didn't say it.

We entered ×× Company, and some boring polite talk covered up these words.

The Courage of Writers 217

— Bai Lai

Every writer with a sense of justice always mercilessly reveals the lining of reality: light or darkness; friends or enemies; in between, he never injects any embellishment or compromise.

However, for this reason, all the poverty and misery and tragic endings are always lurking around every writer with a sense of justice. From this phenomenon, it is clear how important the ability for a great writer to sacrifice is.

On the other hand, everyone knows that the road of writing is the most difficult. Especially in China, let alone the unknown writers; even the rewards of famous writers cannot liberate them from a life of poverty, as is well known. If we are planning for personal gain, needless to say, embarking on the road of writing is the most unfortunate thing.

There must be such writers; not to mention that they will not resent or be discouraged by the trivial hardships of daily life... Even if a great disaster befalls them, they can still bear it with the spirit of martyrdom; only such writers can truly understand the solemn meaning of the cause they are engaged in. And only such writers are worthy of being the drummers of the times.

Reading Zhao Qiuling's Ci Poems 218

— Yang Shiji

I happened to read Zhao Qiuling's "Lamenting the West Wind in Chongqing," sent to Gui Danshu (Jin Lü Gao): "Mocking life is like filling a hole with dirt, wine cannot wash it away. Every chess piece is a wrong move from the start, it's a mistake to study so hard, binding so many feelings!" I couldn't help but feel the same, so I didn't overlook this author like I did other Ci poets of the Qing Dynasty.

Zhao Qiuling's achievements are not particularly high, and the number of genuinely good works in his entire collection is very small, but in terms of the sincerity of his temperament, he is a rare figure in the Qing Dynasty. Even comparing him to Nalan Rongruo, he doesn't pale in comparison, because one is bold and unrestrained, and the other is gentle and melancholy, and I personally happen to prefer the bold and unrestrained sentiment. Qiuling's collection is not difficult to find in today's market, but very few people know Qiuling's name, which I find strange; but why is it strange? Qiuling once said in his inscription on Chen Xiaolu's collection (Jin Lü Qu): "It's a pity that the brush formation sweeps away a thousand people, but it's an ancient and common occurrence in the middle of it; the gauze hat in the Ci poetry arena. Whether it is passed down or not is purely accidental; are those who are passed down all masterpieces? Only the enlightened ones laugh it off. Such a talented person is unfairly erased, imagine how many are buried in obscurity. Just a commoner, who understands him!"

Regarding Qiuling's life story, from the prefaces and postscripts of his collection and the notes of his friend Liang Jinzhu, I only know that his courtesy name was Qingxi, and he was from Renhe. Born in 1803 (Jiaqing Xinwei). He passed the provincial examination in his youth, but did not enter the imperial academy. He then went to Hubei, where he published a volume of "Chu You Cao"; after returning home, he made a living by tutoring, living a life of disappointment for twenty years... He died as a guest in Lingnan in his second year of travel, and his works were burned in a fire. His female friend Wu Pingxiang compiled "Xiang Xiao Jiu Li Ci Qu" into separate volumes. However, I also know that he had the most common background of contemporary literati, that is, poverty, arrogance, weariness of the teaching life, and complaints of not being recognized, so his Ci poems are full of emotion. Like the second poem sent to Gui Danshu:

"It's almost Mid-Autumn again. Facing the blue sky, alas, I've failed to enjoy the round days; the cassia and osmanthus, and the flower fairies of Xiaoshan, all people in my eyes are thousands of miles away. It evokes countless tastes of separation. Swallows fly here and fly away again; I still remember what happened last year. My old garden is unharmed in the west wind, but I have failed to enjoy the willow trees, flowers and wine of the Six Bridges. How saddened is Axian with empty walls; it's hard to start a conversation about home, only reporting that the year is peaceful. I can't bear to beg for food again, lacking the skills to roam the world; poetry and wine, what's the use!"

The sorrow of a declining literati is generally written here.

Qiuling's Ci poems are explicit and clear when describing the scenery, and they have a unique charm, like the verses in "Traveling to Gaoting" (Tai Cheng Lu): "Lightly moving the wine boat, holding a new fishing rod, I learn the life of an old fisherman. Flowers bloom on the ridge, watching the wind pass and shake the coolness, the water marks are all purple. The houses on both sides, the paintings of Changmen close, it is the silkworm market. The green apricots on the branches are still small, only the mulberry shade and the pods are as fat as lard. The soil is slippery and the frogs are level, the shirt is remembered by the fan, and then passing the mountain temple in the setting sun." It vividly depicts the scenery of Jiangnan in late spring and early summer, which cannot be described as anything but genuine.

Qiuling also wrote flowery and ornate language when he was young. His small poems, his poems, and his songs mostly belong to this aspect. Those who liked it praised it as "entering and exiting the flowers," or "following the traces of Wen Tingyun and Li Shangyin," but this is precisely what we do not approve of. When he was in Hubei, his betrothed died, and he once wrote "Xu Li Sao Zhao Hun Ku Zhi," with the last verse (Huan Xi Sha) saying: "Checking my green shirt, there are tear stains, the most heartbreaking thing is ten years ago, drizzle and dusk everywhere. The parrot poem is a genius' blood, the peach blossom is a maiden's soul, I wonder where to mourn Xiang Jun." This is most representative of his work in the transitional phase of imitation.

Qiuling was devoted to friendship and made many friends. He and his friends, such as Liang Puzhu, Yao Gufen, Chen Xiaolu, and Xu Baochan, all had the same preferences, the same views, and the same experiences regarding literature. Later, they scattered and fell apart, and his situation naturally goes without saying. Qiuling has a letter to Liang Jinzhu, describing the various things before and after their separation. The last paragraph is extremely moving. I excerpt it here: "After middle age, life is filled with sorrow and no joy. I often think of the poetry society at your house and the wine society at Yao's house fifteen years ago, drinking freely and selecting rhymes, arranging banquets and judging flowers, believing that this joy was something our generation had not exhausted. Unexpectedly, in the blink of an eye, we've drifted apart like this! Old travels are like dreams, I regret not climbing to the top of Phoenix Mountain, scratching my head and asking the sky. However, if there are two of us in this world, this joy is still possible. I only hope that you cherish yourself on the edge of the world, I also do the same. All the friends in my hometown, Su Yun has not been seen, Minfu was seen once in April, and Fulu would like to see each other but cannot, Shusheng is often seen, Xun Yuan will never be seen again, Jinzhu can only be seen in books."

Qiuling and his friends were not famous in their time, and they could not avoid being full of complaints. Like Qiuling's inscription on Xu Baozhuang's collection (Bai Zi Ling), there are sentences like "There is hatred in this, it's hard to find a confidant in life!" "It's okay to speak madly, you all got your names for nothing!" We can know their indignation. Judging impartially, Qiuling and others can be considered authors who were reasonably independent in the Qing Dynasty poetry scene, and from his sentence "Blaming everyone for imitating Song and then imitating Tang, wrapping up like a stiff silkworm," we can see their eagerness to be independent. He also has a sentence praising Chen Xiaolu: "The whole page is filled with the shadows of white seedlings and autumn water, and the spirit of fallen flowers and mountain forests, beyond Su Shi, Liu Yong, Qin Guan, and Huang Tingjian." I think it's appropriate to use these few sentences as the conclusion to describe him here, it will definitely not be an overestimation or inappropriate.

Just Published 219

Jin Jiu's Dad 220

— Zigang

Since last spring, Jin Jiu's dad began to cough strangely.

He was a middle-aged man, tall, with a neck that was also so long, setting off an even smaller waist. Whether he was wearing a single jacket or a short cotton coat, he always wore a blue cloth belt around his waist. His eating tools were a large box of wooden figures and a stage with a blue cloth curtain underneath. The blue cloth curtain was just enough for Jin Jiu's dad to fit in. While he was tossing those small wooden figures, he was shouting and singing with a hoarse voice, sometimes sharp and piercing, sometimes scratchy like a broken Huqin without rosin.

Every day, he carried the heavy load and wandered through the alleys, knocking on a small gong, looking for customers along some unfamiliar or familiar alleys. Sometimes, he would walk past the doors of some houses with children and tempt them to watch the puppet show every day. Jin Jiu's dad would be scolded by some women, who blamed him for coming every day to trick them out of their copper coins.

"It's already fallen to the price of thirty coins per show!"

Although he argued like that, Jin Jiu's dad still had to lower his head and slip away down another street. He breathed lightly, calculating the exchange rate. In previous years, when it was 30 strings per silver dollar, one show cost 4 strings, which was a little more than one dime. Now it was more than 50 strings per dollar.

"The more effort, the poorer I get!" Thinking like that, he hurriedly finished performing in one place and wiped the sweat before running to another, hoping to make up for the depreciated money by performing more shows. The few mouths at home hadn't reduced their food intake. However, when he only heard the echo of his own hand knocking on the small gong in the alley and didn't hear the call of an employer, Jin Jiu's dad raised his gray eyes and absentmindedly thought:

"Everyone seems to be poor."

However, he also clearly remembered that when he crossed a major road to change the direction of wandering the alleys, he clearly saw crowds of spectators pouring into the cinemas and theaters like clouds.

Hesitating and puzzled, he lingered, with his anxious heart selling his skills. Sometimes he would let a few coins go, or else he would perform a few more scenes to make up for it.

"Dudu, Aiyo..."

Singing with all his might, interspersed with dialogues, his plays often included "Grandma Wang Sawing the Jar" and "Pigsy Sweeping Women," and sometimes he would also mention "Romance of the Three Kingdoms."

Jin Jiu's dad's back gradually bent down, and his slender neck stretched out. His voice became even more hoarse, but when he saw Jin Jiu next to his mother complaining that he wasn't full with the cornbread, he made a black mark in his heart, muttering that he would perform two more shows tomorrow so that the family could have a few more cornbreads to eat.

He extended his working hours, spending less time at home in the morning playing with wooden figures with his child, and not returning until it was dark at night.

Feeling that he was getting weaker and weaker, and that his legs would be tired and sore in less than half a day, Jin Jiu's dad cursed himself inwardly, saying that he was still a middle-aged man! However, what he couldn't hide was the dizziness after walking too much. Once, after performing two times in a row, he stumbled and fell on the carrying pole, and his eyes went dark for a moment, almost falling down.

Slowly, the coughing came, just a little bit in the throat, but it took a lot of effort.

The woman noticed this phenomenon.

The man shook his head: "Caught a cold!"

He couldn't hide it from the woman's sharp eyes. She had seen neighbors with this illness, and who had died because of this illness. Something threatened her:

"Consumption!"

She rang the bell at the Guandi Temple.

She also got a free prescription from somewhere and gave it to the man to drink with water. (To be continued)

Notice: "High Altitude" was originally a long article. What was published a few days ago was only part of it. Because the original text was too long, it will no longer be published. This is a special statement. —Editor.
