Special Issue on Telecommunications

The Voice of the Telecommunications Industry

Direct Cable Route Between Guangdong and Hubei 221

— Zhen

In our country, telegrams to and from various places in South China are centered on Guangzhou. The circuit (A) transmitted by cable is: (1) starting from Shanghai, passing through the Shanghai-Fujian direct line to Fuzhou, and then through Xiamen and Shantou to Guangzhou. (2) Starting from Hankou, passing through Jiujiang, Nanchang, Ganzhou, crossing the Dayuling Mountains to Shaozhou, and then to Guangzhou. (3) Starting from Hankou, passing through Changsha, Hengzhou, Chenzhou, Shaozhou, and then to Guangzhou; or passing through Hengzhou, Yongzhou, Guilin, Wuzhou to Guangzhou. (B) There are two ways of transmitting by wireless telegraph: (1) Direct line between Guangdong and Hubei, (2) Direct line between Shanghai and Guangzhou. (C) The line transmitted by submarine cable is provided by the foreign-owned Great Northern Telegraph Company, which reaches Hong Kong through the Shanghai-Hong Kong submarine cable, and then transfers to Guangzhou. This is the general situation of the South China circuit.

It is found that the above-mentioned cable circuits have been destroyed by bandits and communists and have been in disrepair for many years. The direct line between Guangdong and Hubei (via the Guangxun Han circuit) has been blocked for more than 20 years. The remaining routes are fragmented and have never been opened for direct communication. In recent years, the pole lines in the three provinces of Hunan, Fujian, and Jiangxi have been repaired in time due to military progress, but the construction is crude and the work is not strong, so it cannot be directly communicated. Transferring telegrams delays time. If it is interrupted by weather or bandits, it is even more of a delay. Therefore, in the past, domestic merchants sent telegrams to South China, and because of their accuracy and reliability, they were more willing to pay the submarine cable fee and transfer them through the Shanghai-Hong Kong submarine cable. For decades, the loss of interests has been incalculable! After the establishment of wireless telegraph stations in Shanghai, Hankou, and Guangzhou, and the opening of direct lines between Shanghai-Guangdong and Guangdong-Hubei, many rights and interests were recovered. However, due to the limited capacity of the generators, if all the telegrams from South China are transferred through the two lines, it is actually difficult to do so, and it will inevitably lead to congestion and delays.

In order to facilitate north-south telecommunications, the Ministry of Communications has selected the fastest route between Guangdong and Hubei (ie, the Changheng Shaoguang line), actively reorganized it, and added pole lines to achieve direct communication. The lines in Jiangxi and Fujian provinces are also being repaired. The Hunan-Guangdong line project started in June last year. It was disrupted by the Jiangxi bandits intruding into Hunan. It was completed in January this year. The direct line between Guangdong and Hubei was reported on February 11, and the results are very good. The telegrams coming and going are fast and accurate. The line blocked for more than 20 years between Guangdong and Hubei is now opened and completed by Hunan Province. From now on, news from South China will reach the Central Plains in an instant, which will make a great contribution to national communications.

Thoughts After Reorganizing the Old Debts of the Telecommunications Administration 222

— Chu Hao

During the era of the Ministry of Communications of the former Beijing government, various telecommunications debt loans were successively borrowed from foreign merchants in Japan, Britain, Germany, the United States, and other countries. The amount was huge. The contract terms were extremely harsh, the interest rate was high, and there were even provisions for paying interest in advance. Over the years, the Ministry of Communications has been unable to meet the telecommunications debt repayments. The amount of foreign debt repaid was very small. Not to mention the principal, even the interest paid was less than one-tenth. As a result, the principal and interest were compounded, and the debt increased day by day. As of the end of 1934, the total debt, including principal and interest, converted into national currency at the current gold price, totaled more than 80 million yuan. All the chief officials of the Ministry of Communications have been wary of this debt and have not been able to find a solution to reorganize it. Since Zhu Jia-hua took office as the head of the department, he realized that this debt had been pending for a long time, and the principal and interest would accumulate more and more. If a proper method was not devised to solve it as soon as possible, the entire telecommunications industry would go bankrupt. Therefore, with the approval of the Executive Yuan, personnel were dispatched to handle the matter. After several months of negotiations, new repayment methods were separately agreed with each creditor. The creditors gave up all their inherent rights. This kind of understanding attitude is worthy of our praise, and Marco Min's representative said that it is based on the Sino-British Gengkuan method, which can promote diplomatic relations between the two countries, which is especially sincere. Therefore, the result of this debt reorganization is not only that the principal and interest are repaid, but also tens of millions of yuan are saved compared with the old contract, and the diplomatic relations of our country have also been greatly improved. It cannot be said that it is not an extraordinary event in our telecommunications industry in recent years! The detailed methods have been recorded in various newspapers, so I will not repeat them here. I am writing my feelings to provide research for those who are concerned about the telecommunications industry.

The Ministry of Communications' accumulated old debts for various telecommunications projects are the crux of the telecommunications economy's inability to consolidate, and the pain and constraints suffered by our telecommunications industry for more than ten years have been the most severe. Although all the previous telecommunications authorities knew that the telecommunications future would not be secured unless the above-mentioned old debts were resolved, the debts were too large and there was no way to reorganize them. Therefore, although demands for repayment were pressing, they were always dealt with through evasive and delaying means as a temporary measure. Little did they know that creditors and debts are clearly stipulated by law, and when it comes to foreign merchants, it is related to international credit. If you are not careful in dealing with it occasionally, and do not seek fundamental solutions, the impact will be unimaginable.

In the contracts for various telecommunications loans, such as the loan contract for expanding telephone collaboration signed by the Old Ministry of Communications and the Sino-Japanese Industrial Company, and the joint venture between the Western Electric Company and the China Electric Company, there are provisions for priority in purchasing materials. Since the methods were contradictory, disputes arose as a result; for example, if materials were ordered from Company A, Company B would come out and interfere on the grounds of priority rights. If materials were ordered from Company B, Company A would also raise objections on the same grounds. If materials were purchased from material merchants other than Companies A and B, the accusations would be even heavier. All of these kinds of things, the Ministry of Communications often had the pain of being unable to cope with. And because the debts had not been repaid for a long time and credit was lost, the company often secretly increased the price of materials. The Ministry of Communications, due to contractual relations, although it knew the loss clearly, had to endure the pain and accept it. Therefore, the loss on telecommunications materials purchased over the years cannot be counted, this is one. Furthermore, the successive telecommunications authorities were concerned about the telecommunications debt, but since the debt had never been reorganized, there was no accurate figure. It was unknown to what extent the accumulated debt was. Therefore, the entire telecommunications budget could not be established. And because of the harsh conditions of the various contracts, various new facilities were restricted, which led to repeated obstacles and made it difficult to develop. This is two. Among the various telecommunications debts, the largest amount and the most serious nature are: One is the loan for expanding and improving cable telegraph engineering costs borrowed from the Japanese merchant Dongya Xingye Co., Ltd. by the former Ministry of Communications on February 10, 1920, totaling 10,222,020 yen and 47 sen, with the entire property of the cable telegraph as collateral. One is the loan for expanding telephone borrowed from the Sino-Japanese Industrial Company by the Old Ministry of Communications in October 1918, totaling 10 million yen, which was mortgaged with the existing and future expanded telephone property and application rights. Later, the Old Ministry of Communications continued to purchase materials from the company and increased the amount owed by approximately 6.5 million yen. Although the above two loans have been repaid by the Ministry of Communications one after another, the amount is very small, insufficient to pay the interest. Therefore, as of the end of last year, the accumulated principal and interest combined exceeded more than twice the principal. If this situation continues indefinitely, it will inevitably accumulate more and more. If the creditors feel that the debt cannot be recovered, and their grief and anger come together, and they turn to rely on the power of their country to demand the disposal of the collateral, we really have no way to deal with it. Looking to the future, we cannot help but tremble with fear, this is three.

With these three reasons, I know that although the telecommunications authorities have worked hard with an indomitable spirit in recent years, heading towards the road of reform and revitalization, everyone's hearts are uneasy with the huge debt in front of them and the crises all around. Now all the debts have been satisfactorily resolved, and the harsh conditions have been completely abolished, which is no different from someone who has been shackled for a long time being freed. The joy and comfort cannot be described in words! From now on, the thorns have been cleared away, the hidden worries have been eliminated, and all kinds of plans can be carried out step by step without any worries or constraints. Therefore, the clearing of telecommunications debts has a epoch-making significance in the entire telecommunications history, and the far-sighted and brilliant insights and the wise and decisive spirit of the current authorities are worthy of admiration and praise.

From now on, I sincerely hope that all sectors of society will share the difficulties and dangers and contribute their sincerity. For the previously owed telephone bills, they should find ways to repay them, and for all future telecommunications fees, they must pay in cash as required. The telecommunications economy can be revived, and the debt reorganization plan formulated by the Ministry of Communications this time will not be interrupted. The future of the country will rely on it, and it is not just the telecommunications industry!

The Process and Impact of Signing the Shanghai Long-Distance Telephone Connection Contract 223

— Cang Zhou

Local telephones and long-distance telephones, one is for short-distance communication, and the other is for long-distance communication. Both have their own effects. However, long-distance telephones cannot develop without local telephones as their intermediary, and local telephones must have long-distance telephones for their promotion before their functions become more apparent. They must cooperate closely, like vehicles relying on each other, to reach a situation where one can speak to someone thousands of miles away as if they were in the same room.

Shanghai is the largest port in our country, holding the hub of national commerce and finance. Surrounding it are southern Jiangsu and northern Zhejiang, and there are many political and commercial cities. Therefore, the connection and communication between local telephones and long-distance telephones in Shanghai is extremely necessary. However, long-distance telephones are operated by the Ministry of Communications, and local telephones in the concession are operated by foreign merchants. The different operating entities cause the connection problem to arise.

The connection between local telephones in the Shanghai concession and long-distance telephones began in May 1926, when the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications signed a long-distance telephone contract with the Shanghai China and Foreign Telephone Company. This contract was based on the Sino-Foreign Telephone Communication Contract signed in 1925. Regarding the charging method, it was stipulated that company users using long-distance telephones, regardless of whether they were calling out or calling in, the company could charge an additional 5 dimes per call as a handling fee. In May 1932, the contract expired. The Ministry of Communications immediately sent personnel to negotiate with the Shanghai Telephone Company (which inherited the China and Foreign Telephone Company to operate the concession telephone) to renew the new contract. However, since the Sino-Foreign Telephone Communication Contract on which the original contract was based had expired and a new contract had not yet been signed, it was inconvenient to resolve the long-distance telephone connection contract first, and this case was shelved. Until April 1933, the temporary contract for telephones in the Chinese and Concession areas was officially signed, and the Ministry of Communications sent personnel to continue negotiations with the company, but there was no result for a long time.

The signing of the new contract this time was initiated by the Shanghai Telephone Bureau's request to increase relay lines. The long-distance telephone traffic in Shanghai has developed extremely far, and the concession accounts for 80 to 90 percent of it. There are currently 15 pairs of long-distance lines connected to the Shanghai Long-Distance Station: 5 pairs along the Beijing-Shanghai Railway line, 6 pairs along the Beijing-Shanghai Highway line, 2 pairs along the Shanghai-Hangzhou line, and 2 pairs along the Shanghai-Songjiang line. There are only 8 pairs of relay lines between China and the concession. It can be imagined that 8 pairs of relay lines are not enough to handle 15 pairs of long-distance lines. The Shanghai Telephone Bureau repeatedly requested the telephone company to increase the number of relay lines. The telephone company proposed the issue of contract renewal, and believed that the increase in relay lines was a prerequisite, so the negotiations continued. The point of contention between the two parties was the company's method of sharing telephone fees. The Ministry of Communications wanted to maintain the original plan, that is, the company would share 5 cents per call regardless of incoming or outgoing calls. The company wanted to share 15% of the total telephone fees for outgoing calls, with a minimum of 10 cents and a maximum of 1 yuan and 50 cents, and 5% for incoming calls, with a minimum of 5 cents and a maximum of 1 yuan and 50 cents. Finally, both parties compromised and agreed that the company would receive 10% for outgoing calls and 5% for incoming calls, with the minimum and maximum limits being 5 cents and 1 yuan and 50 cents respectively. On the 7th of this month, the telephone bureau and the telephone company officially signed the contract.

The results of signing the contract: The most important ones are the addition of relay lines and the increase in the company's share of fees. According to the current long-distance telephone traffic in Shanghai, the Beijing-Shanghai line is the busiest. The Ministry of Communications built new long-distance lines along the highway in the shortest possible time, originally hoping that the Beijing-Shanghai telephone traffic could be expedited. However, after the new line was completed, the Beijing-Shanghai telephone traffic was still congested. Since the long-distance relay lines in Shanghai could not be increased, the newly added Beijing-Shanghai line was just a formality. Now that the new contract has been signed, the number of relay lines can be increased, and the telephone traffic in all directions will definitely be smooth. Secondly, regarding the company's share of telephone fees, the telephone company's hopes were quite extravagant this time. Although the Ministry of Communications negotiated and reduced the fees, the final result was quite different from the original plan. In the future, the handling fees paid by the Ministry of Communications to the telephone company every month will undoubtedly increase significantly. However, the Ministry of Communications emphasizes increasing revenue. The two parties have different goals.

Joint Political and Military Organs Suppress Private Use of Official Telegrams 224

— Reporter

I have read Traffic Gazette No. 617, which contains a letter from the Political Training Department of the Nanchang Headquarters of the Military Affairs Commission to the Ministry of Transportation, stating roughly: "We received a letter stating that the Political Training Department of the 11th Division used the official telegraph paper of this department to send private telegrams, requesting an investigation, admonishment, and a general order for suppression, etc., along with a copy of the original telegram; this is confirmed. The individual surnamed Li (the reporter withholds the name for now) who privately used official telegrams has been dismissed and is under investigation. This department has already issued a general order to suppress private use of official telegrams," etc. It also contains a telegraph from the Western Route Headquarters of the Bandit Suppression Army of Jiangxi, Guangdong, Fujian, Hunan, and Hubei, dated November of last year, stating: "We previously received a telegraph stating that the Changsha Telegraph Bureau detained two official telegrams related to private matters from Chaling, requesting an investigation to identify the sender and issue a reprimand, etc. We immediately telegraphed Army Commander Liu Jianxu to investigate and reply. Now, according to Army Commander Liu's reply telegraph, 'We have respectfully received your telegraph and have complied with your order to reprimand the sender and instructed subordinates not to send private telegrams again. We hereby report this,' etc." Reading this letter and telegram, we can see how seriously the current political and military authorities regard telecommunications laws and regulations.

It has long been the case that private matters cannot be sent using official telegrams. The National Government issued a general order to all political and military organs to comply with this in the 18th year of the Republic [1929], and the Ministry of Transportation also stipulated methods and announced them to the public. However, two years ago, during times of military urgency, officials in various political and military organs were unaware of telecommunications laws and regulations. They often used printed telegram paper to send official telegrams for private matters. When confronted, they became aggressive and intimidating. If the telegram was detained and not sent, they would roar and even threaten with "delaying military operations." Telegraph bureau personnel, subjected to their coercion, had no choice but to temporarily accept and send the telegrams, while reporting to the Ministry of Transportation for instructions. Official correspondence took time. By the time the Ministry's reply arrived, the official had already been transferred elsewhere with the agency. Seeing that they could use force to send private official telegrams at Telegraph Bureau A, the official would do the same at Telegraph Bureau B or C. Gradually, they came to regard it as a right enjoyed by military personnel, lending printed telegram paper to non-military personnel for sending telegrams. Unscrupulous staff members in the bureau used printed telegram paper in place of merchants' telegrams. All sorts of abuses arose, becoming a common practice. The losses from telegram fees were incalculable. This situation was especially prevalent during times of military activity or in remote locations, as this reporter has repeatedly witnessed.

In recent years, the Ministry of Transportation has strictly suppressed private use of official telegrams and stipulated measures for reporting bureaus, intermediate bureaus, and receiving bureaus to investigate and detain private telegrams, along with rewards and penalties. Telegraph bureau personnel also consider suppressing private telegrams to be an essential measure for streamlining telecommunications administration and are working hard to implement it with remarkable results. The following is a table listing the number of private telegrams detained in each district in the 21st and 22nd years of the Republic [1932 and 1933]:

Table of Private Telegrams Detained in Each District in the 21st and 22nd Years of the Republic.

From the above, it can be seen that private official telegrams cannot escape investigation and detention. Now, with the assistance of political and military organs, offenders will be dismissed and investigated. Political and military personnel will realize that this type of telegram will certainly be detained and that sending it will certainly be punished. They will not risk significant losses for petty gains. Private official telegrams may disappear from telegraph bureaus altogether.

The Use of Roman Alphabet Telegraph Codes 225

— Qinghua

—Attention Overseas Compatriots—

The "Newly Compiled Clear and Cipher Telegraph Codes" published by the Ministry of Transportation contains a type of Roman alphabet telegraph code (i.e., Western language telegraph code) in addition to the more common telegraph code books sold on the market. Each three letters represents one Chinese character. The only advantage of this code is that it saves on telegram fees. Overseas compatriots sending telegrams to their home country can save 64% on telegram fees, which is more economical than using Western language telegrams. Examples are provided below:

For example, the five characters "Goods arrived, remit payment quickly." If sent using Chinese four-character codes, they would be translated as 6303 0451 2949 6643 0565, a total of five codes. Each code is charged at the full price of one character. Assuming the price per character is one yuan, the fee would be five yuan. If sent using the Roman alphabet telegraph code, the five characters can be translated as RAO ARJ HUS SGL AVT, five codes. Then, these five codes are combined into RAOARJHUSSGIAV and divided into three codes, five letters each: RAOAR JHUSS GIAVT. These three codes are charged as three characters and are eligible for a 60% discount, resulting in a fee of only 1.80 yuan. Comparing the two methods, the difference in telegram fees is 3.20 yuan, demonstrating the benefits of using the Roman alphabet telegraph code.

However, users of this code must pay attention to the following points:

1. Before sending telegrams to relatives, friends, or related businesses, purchase several copies of the "Newly Compiled Clear and Cipher Telegraph Codes" published by the Ministry of Transportation and give them to relatives, friends, or people with whom you intend to exchange telegrams, and inform them of the usage of this code (the book contains instructions). It is best to try translating it once by mail to avoid misunderstandings.

2. This code can only be used for the telegram text. The names and addresses of the recipients in the telegram should still be in Western or Chinese clear code to ensure that the telegraph bureau can deliver the telegram.

3. If a telegram is sent from abroad to the home country and the sender has not notified the recipient to use this code in advance, the word "PDAIN" can be added before the telegram text to indicate that the telegram is in Roman alphabet telegraph code. Upon receipt, the telegraph bureau will translate it into text according to the Chinese clear code telegram procedure and deliver it. However, this is limited to telegrams from abroad, as foreign telegraph bureaus are not responsible for translation.

4. If the telegram text contains only four characters, it will be translated into twelve Roman letters (three letters per character). Then, divide it into codes of five letters each, resulting in two codes, with two letters remaining. These two letters can also be treated as one code, as Western language codes must not exceed five letters per code. If there are fewer than five letters, it can also be treated as one code.

5. The "Newly Compiled Clear and Cipher Telegraph Codes" compiled and printed by the Ministry of Transportation is priced at 20 cents per copy. Local telegraph bureaus and radio stations sell them. If they are sold out, you can write directly to the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Transportation in Nanjing to purchase them. If you have any questions about the code, you can write directly to this newspaper, and we will provide a detailed reply.

6. Domestic telegrams do not have a 60% discount for Western language codes, and Western language telegrams are more expensive than Chinese telegrams. For example, the five characters "Goods arrived, remit payment quickly" cost only 50 cents at the Chinese rate. If converted into a three-character Western language code, it would cost 60 cents, which is uneconomical. Therefore, it is not advisable to use this code.

Convenience of Sending Telegrams via Telephone 226

— Baozhen

The Ministry of Transportation has established "Measures for Receiving and Sending Telegrams via City Telephone" to facilitate telegram reception and sending for city telephone users, which has been implemented since February 1st of last year. According to these measures, city telephone users who wish to use the telephone to receive and send telegrams can apply for registration at the local telegraph bureau or radio station, agree on a password, and prepay enough fees for half a month of telegrams before starting to receive and send telegrams. (However, telephone users who do not wish to send telegrams by telephone do not need to prepay telegram fees.) These measures are thorough and well-planned, and are very convenient for telephone users who exchange a lot of telegrams. However, telephone users who exchange fewer telegrams may find the registration fee and prepayment of telegram fees a little troublesome. If they do not follow these procedures, the telegraph bureau or radio station cannot accommodate them due to the regulations. Therefore, while these measures are convenient for telephone users who exchange a lot of telegrams, they are not universally available to ordinary telephone users.

Recently, the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Transportation has introduced "Measures for Telephone Bureau Users to Send Telegrams via Telephone" (see the February 10th Shen Bao) to address the above shortcomings. The telephone bureau has installed two telephones in the telegraph bureau's telegraph room for the exclusive use of the telegraph bureau to listen to telegrams sent by telephone users. According to these measures, city telephone users do not need to register with the local telegraph bureau or radio station. They only need to agree on a password and prepay telegram fees. They can dial telephone number ××××× (the dedicated telephone installed in the telegraph bureau's telegraph room) at any time to speak with the telegraph bureau's receiving operator and send telegrams. After the telegraph bureau's receiving operator has finished recording the telegram, they can assign a telegraph number and send it to the operator on duty according to the route the telegram should take to its destination. The procedure is extremely fast. The required telegram fee can be temporarily recorded by the telegraph bureau, and the telephone bureau will collect it from the user at the end of the month, which is even more convenient. From now on, telephone users can send telegrams at any time without leaving their homes, which is extremely simple and convenient. It is reported that these measures are being piloted in Shanghai and Tianjin first. Once they prove effective, they will be implemented in other major cities. This reporter hopes that in the future, telephone users in major cities will all be able to send telegrams at any time using the telephone, so that the two communication tools of telephone and telegraph can work together to serve the public more effectively. Please contact your local telegraph bureau for details of these measures.

Reply to Mr. Gu Qun's Inquiry from Shanghai 227

— Baozhen

This newspaper received a letter from Mr. Gu inquiring about the method of calculating fees for Western language telegrams. We hereby provide separate answers to the questions raised:

Question: (1) I used to send many Western language international telegrams when I was in Beiping. For all these telegrams, the recipient's name and address were often written as Chineselegation or Sinolegation, which were always charged as one word, regardless of the country to which the telegram was sent. Why is it that recently, when sending Western language telegrams from Shanghai to Beiping and other countries, the telegraph bureau charges each of the following words used in the recipient's name and address: Britishlegation, Frenchlegation, Spanishlegation, Sinolegation, etc., as two words? What is the basis for this? Please explain.

Answer: According to regulations, words written together in Western language telegrams should be charged separately, unless they can be proven to be registered telegraphic addresses, whether in the address, text, or signature. The words Britishlegation, Frenchlegation, Spanishlegation, Sinolegation, Chineselegation, etc., used in the recipient's name and address of the Western language telegrams you sent from Shanghai to Beiping and other countries, are words written together and are not the registered telegraphic addresses of the recipients. (Our embassies abroad have the registered telegraphic address Sinolegate. The registered telegraphic addresses of the British Embassy in China are Prodrome and Britatin. The registered telegraphic address of the French Embassy in China is Legafrance. The registered telegraphic address of the Spanish Embassy is not known.) Because the Roman letters contained in these words are all more than ten, they clearly conflict with the section of the regulations regarding telegraphic addresses for Western language telegrams that states, "Telegraphic addresses for Western language telegrams are limited to a maximum of ten Roman letters." There may be some misunderstanding in your letter. Perhaps the international telegrams you sent in Beiping used the registered telegraphic address Sinolegate instead of the recipient's name and address, and not the words written together Sinolegation, Chineselegation. Therefore, the telegraph bureau charged according to the regulations as one word. For the telegrams sent from Shanghai to Beiping and other countries, the words written together Sinolegation, Chineselegation, etc., used as the recipient's name and address, should be charged as two words according to the regulations. The telegraph bureau's request for additional fees is in accordance with Section 9, Paragraph 1 of Article 18 of Chapter 6 of the Telegraph Regulations attached to the International Telecommunications Convention, "Words that are combined or altered and violate the customary usage of the language to which they belong shall not be permitted." (To be continued)

Bi-Weekly News 228

— Fellow of the Newspaper

Shanghai and Tianjin Open Telephone Telegram Service

To facilitate telephone users in Shanghai and Tianjin in sending telegrams, the Ministry of Transportation has formulated telephone telegram measures. Telephone users in Shanghai and Tianjin can use telephones to send telegrams at any time without prior registration or deposit. The procedure is simple and convenient. When a user sends a telegram, they only need to dial the telephone number specified by the telegraph bureau (Shanghai Telephone Bureau specifies South City 21193 and 21194). After the call is connected, they report the telephone number and registered name, and then hang up the telephone and wait for the telegraph bureau to call. When the call is connected, the telegraph bureau will ask for the name once and then read out the telegram word by word or code by code. After the telegraph bureau records the telegram word by word, it will repeat it once. If the proofreading is correct, the telegram will be sent. After the telegram is sent, a copy of the telegram with the amount of the telegram fee to be paid will be sent to the original telegraph sender for review, signature and stamp and then the messenger will bring the copy back to the telegraph bureau for record, and all telegram fees payable will be collected at the end of the month. This measure allows the telegram sender to send telegrams without leaving home. Its convenience is comparable to that of European and American countries. This shows that the telecommunications authorities have recently been striving to commercialize the telegraph business. (Detailed measures can be obtained from the Shanghai or Tianjin Telegraph Bureau)

Measures for Charging Telegram Copy Fees

If there are more than two recipients in the same place, the sender can send a telegram with copies to save money. This type of telegram is charged as one telegram, but a copy fee must be charged. The copy fee was originally calculated according to the number of copies added. For example, if there are three recipients, then a copy fee of three copies will be charged. If each copy is 20 cents, the fee will be 60 cents. However, according to Article 61 of the current International Telegraph Regulations, the copy fee should be calculated according to the number of recipients. For example, if three copies are sent, the fee will be 60 cents. The reason for this is that the receiving telegraph bureau does not send a complete copy of the incoming telegram when sending the telegram. According to the regulations, three copies of the incoming telegram paper should be prepared, and each copy should only contain the name and address of one recipient and the text of the telegram, so that the recipient does not know that the sender has also sent the telegram to others. Therefore, the telegraph bureau's procedures are indeed to make three copies, not to add two copies. In order to unify the method of charging copy fees for international and domestic telegrams, the Ministry of Communications has ordered all telegraph bureaus to calculate the fees according to the number of copies sent from March 1.

Cancellation of Long-Distance Telephone Deposit

According to regulations, telephone users of each telephone bureau need to pre-pay a deposit when using long-distance telephones to avoid arrears of long-distance call charges. Although this measure provides a relatively stable guarantee for the telephone bureau's charging, it is always inconvenient for users to pre-pay the deposit. In order to facilitate users and promote business development, the Ministry of Communications has ordered the telephone bureaus in the capital city and Shanghai to conduct a pilot project. If the results of the pilot project are very good, the other telephone bureaus will also promote the implementation of the pilot project.

Legislative Yuan Passes International Telecommunication Convention

The International Telecommunication Convention and its related regulations passed by the International Telegraph and Radio Conference in Xijing, Madrid in 1932 should be approved by the governments of each contracting country. After our country signed the convention, the Ministry of Communications submitted the original case to the Executive Yuan for transfer to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation, which has been passed by the Yuan at the first meeting of the fourth session of the Legislative Yuan on February 8, and will be submitted to the National Government for approval in the near future to complete the formalities.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

The Construction of Chinese Culture 229

— Xing An

After reading the "Declaration on the Construction of Chinese Culture with Chinese Standards," we seem to have discovered a glimmer of light in the future of Chinese culture!

When the British literary giant George Bernard Shaw traveled to China a few years ago, he made the following criticism of our country's culture: "China has no culture." Does China really have no culture? Is China really a country without culture? What exactly is the meaning of Shaw's statement? What kind of explanation does he give for the nature of culture? We really cannot know!

China is an ancient civilization and a cultural country nurtured by 5,000 years of history! We dare to boast like this. We are not exaggerating in doing so: because Chinese culture occupies a very important position in the field of world culture. However, this is past glory; what kind of situation has it become now?

In that declaration, it is pointed out at the beginning: "In the field of culture, we cannot see present-day China"! This is today's China. Shaw's judgment that "China has no culture" is not without considerable insight. As a result, the Chinese people feel depressed, groping around aimlessly, struggling desperately! Some are advocating "restoration" and drilling into the tombs of the ancients, trying to beg for inspiration from skeletons: some are clamoring for "welcoming the new", vying for the dregs of Westernization, hoping to pick out a little "life-saving elixir" in the dregs. But the result is the same disappointment!

So, is Chinese culture just going to be allowed to perish like this? Absolutely not! Although Chinese culture is now mired in an atmosphere of smog and desolation: we should embrace a firm and fearless spirit, overcome all difficulties, and build a new culture from this atmosphere! To engage in the construction of a new culture, we should make efforts in three aspects: reviewing the past of China, grasping the present of China, and building the future of China.

The new culture of China is a culture with Chinese standards. This kind of culture should be in line with the times and the environment, and it should be suitable for our needs. A group of restorationists believe that all ancient thoughts and systems are beautiful and good: so they advocate that everything should take the ancient as the model, which neglects the sense of the times. As for those who advocate embracing the new, they believe that all new and strange things in Europe and the United States are excellent: we should imitate them as much as possible. This again neglects the sense of space. It must be known that ancient culture has good and evil: European and American culture has advantages and disadvantages. And the choice of a kind of cultural relic suitable for ancient culture, and the absorption of European and American culture, are those that are the essence and meet the needs of the times and the environment. Then preserve it and take it: those that are rough and unsuitable for the needs of the times and the environment, then abolish it and discard it. This is what those who bear the responsibility of building China's new culture in the future must pay attention to.

We hope that after the successful construction of China's new cultural theory, not only will Chinese culture be able to restore its past glory and stand side by side with foreign countries; it will also be able to make valuable contributions to world culture!

New Fengchun 230

— Si Quan

New Fengchun is the Beijing-Guangzhou general store next door to my house, and it is also the only department store in our town. Lao Guan is an honest merchant who is called a Laughing Buddha—he has been called that since I can remember, and his real surname has gradually been forgotten. In fact, this title is most suitable for him: he is an overweight fat man, and his protruding belly can be victorious over that of a woman about to give birth. On summer nights, he would bare his upper body and cool off in front of the door. When his arms, as thick as small tree roots, waved a palm-leaf fan, the fat on the back of his head and beside his breasts surged like waves. However, the most pictorial part was his pair of eyes that were always squinting into a line and his pair of flat, wide mouths. He came to our town in the first year of the Republic [1912], rented the remaining house of my family's uncle next door, and lived a single life running a small candy stall.

By the time I went home from school every day and used the copper coins my mother gave me to buy candy from his store, it already had the rudimentary form of a rural town general store. He often told the story of his struggle during this period as a moving story: there is a joke in our hometown: those who have not heard the story of Laughing Buddha are not people of our town.

This joke is something Laughing Buddha is proud of: but he is not complacent. After he got married, he and his wife worked even harder and more frugally. I remember very clearly that the black dates I took to school to fill my stomach when I went to high school in the city were also bought from his store. The sign of New Fengchun seemed to have been hung up at that time. According to what he told people himself, the sign was still what he had been using when he set up a stall in the town, but at first it was just used on the back. As for why he brought this sign with him like a treasure, it also evoked a story from him. It was about the year of the Restoration [1912], when he was an apprentice in a southern goods store in Shanghai. On the night of the attack on the arsenal, he saved his life with this sign. The three characters New Fengchun were the sign of his master's store. Many people did not believe this story to be true, but the fact that New Fengchun became famous in our

Page 24

Town is a real fact; and it gradually spread to the surrounding villages. – This naturally also has a reason, because the land and water routes to the city all have to pass through our small town. Sometimes when people met Laughing Buddha going to the city to purchase goods, everyone asked him to bring them something. These things were naturally not available in his store. This inspired Laughing Buddha's cleverness, and he purchased all these things, but the price was the same as in the city. The prosperity of this kind of business can be predicted.

Time flies so fast. After I finished four years of high school (old school system,) New Fengchun was a veritable general store. Everything from five-spice beans, coarse paper, dried bamboo shoots, red and black dates, matches, and all the items needed by rural people, his store did not miss a single item.

Later, I came to Shanghai to study at university, but because of my father's death, my family fell into decline. After dropping out of school, I struggled for food and clothing, and at the same time brought my mother to live with me in Shanghai, so my hometown became isolated and forgotten. At the end of last year, my uncle passed away, and when I returned to my hometown, it was a sunset dusk. Because of the hasty journey, I did not notice the Laughing Buddha with a pair of eyes that were always squinting into a line and a flat, wide mouth. The next day, when my aunt ordered the long-term workers to go to the city to purchase the items used in my uncle's funeral, she remembered him. When asked, the person who answered first shook his head and told me a sad story. In summary, his wife ran away with a man, and Laughing Buddha hanged himself!

Returning to Shanghai with double sorrow, I couldn't help but think of that joke: those who have not heard the story of Laughing Buddha are not people of our town, and the three characters New Fengchun seemed to have taken root and were floating in my mind.

That honest merchant who struggled all his life, now and his business have disappeared from the world!

Spring Suburban Scenery 231

Coconuts and Durians 232

— Man Su

Coconuts and durians are two special products of equatorial lands.

Vast groves are planted with orderly rows of coconut trees. Rows are separated by open spaces. On top of those tall trees, coconuts ripen every month. Chinese or Malay people pick them, and transport them to the market by cart or boat. In the open spaces in front and behind the shops, merchants and vendors agree on a price, and then count "one, two, three, four..." Then, workers break the hard shells, dig out the meat, dry it in the sun, and sell it to oil pressing factories. Coconut meat is pressed into oil, which can be used for lighting lamps, or for women to apply to their hair, or the coconut material can be used to make soap and other items.

A coconut grove is a unique tropical beauty, a comfortable place. Under the scorching sunlight, the coconut grove is exceptionally cool under the large shadows, the cool breeze is refreshing, blowing away the stifling heat. At night, the moon sifts its white light on the ground, the leaves sway with their shadows. The night is shrouded in a mysterious atmosphere, revealing a human paradise.

If one were to build a thatched cottage in the grove, like the owner of the grove, with the foundation of the house built of wood, and the walls built of wooden planks. Leaving windows facing all directions, allowing the cool breeze to blow through the entire house. In the evening, on the veranda by the railing, place a bottle of beer or a cup of coffee, lie down and gaze at the towering trees in the darkness, countless dark clusters; or on a moonlit night, gaze at the moon, dreaming a sweet dream. When the mood strikes, write a poem, read a story, it is truly endless joy, a human paradise.

Moreover, under the coconut trees is often where people in the equator play love games, a place that is not guarded against by any etiquette in the world. This is a naked world, a world of primitive people! Civilized people are useless here.

Therefore, it is very appropriate to use coconuts to represent the spirit and way of life of equatorial people.

○ ○ ○ ○

Durian fruit is covered with thorns and grows in wild forests. When ripe, it emits a huge stench, the smell resembling feces. But it tastes bitter and sweet, and the taste lingers in the mouth for a long time.

Chinese people who first arrive at the pass dare not eat it. But once they get used to eating it, they would "eat durian fruit even if they have to pawn their rags." Just like people who grow up in the plains.

Once durian fruit enters the market, the whole street is filled with the stench. At that time, the shells and kernels are everywhere, and people are eating durian fruit like crazy. Malays are like this, Chinese are like this, and even some Europeans are like this.

Eating durian fruit is quite difficult. Because the shell is hard and full of thorns, one should carefully use a knife to pry it open, and then use hands to dig out the meat from the slices of yellow, sticky flesh. The hands are covered with a pulpy substance, and the mouth exudes a foul odor. However, it is said that eating like this is the most enjoyable.

The way of eating durian fruit is the most common. The best way is: to squat down, regardless of rank or age, scrambling to dig out the meat to eat, surrounding the fruit. Until only the shell is left, then reluctantly leave as if something is lost.

Therefore, even judging from the way of eating durian fruit and the excitement and intoxication of the general public, it is enough to symbolize the spirit and way of life of the equatorial region!

○ ○ ○ ○

Using coconuts and durians as the symbols of the equator is truly the most appropriate.

Luo Yin Yong 233

— Lao Xin

In the names of old places, there are often hidden myths or historical stories. And "Luo Yin Yong" is one of them. This is just a small place, but this small place has a thriving and lively time once a year, and this time is in the hot summer, when the divine women who worship the banners of the gods, and the poets and writers, must pass through it on their way to Dinghu Mountain. Therefore, from the mouths of most friends from Guangdong, you will always hear this poetic place name.

"Luo Yin Yong," how poetic it is. A place like a hermit's dwelling. Here are some farmers, planting dry fields. Although the land is not very good, according to the old custom in the South, they still harvest twice a year without fail. The people are so honest and so simple. Although every year the atmosphere of the city blows in, they never get infected even once. Although the men sometimes gamble, there has never been an accident; and the women are even more diligent, going to the fields to help during the farming season, and going to the mountains to cut grass and chop firewood for fuel when the fields are empty. This poetic place really has a hermit's flavor. When I come down from Dinghu Mountain, I always say goodbye here with a sense of sorrow.

This time, a friend and I went to Dinghu Mountain on a whim in late autumn. After coming down the mountain, we also went to this place as usual to have a snack and rest. There is a small teahouse that sells dim sum and tea, which is prepared for the guests' lunch. Naturally, after the lively season, this place is only coldly lonely. But I especially love this loneliness without the atmosphere of the city, so this time it seems particularly nostalgic. Perhaps it is because after this time, I will have to leave behind everything familiar from the past, and embark on an unfamiliar and lonely wandering journey that I long for. I gazed at everything familiar with my sentimental eyes.

"This small place has changed a bit," I said to my traveling companion. It really is a bit different.

"Naturally, when everything changes, this won't be an exception."

So, I paid more attention to every little thing here.

"The grain prices have fallen. This time, it's really terrible."

"When the harvest is bad, people blame the heavens; when the harvest is good, it's still the same. Who can you blame?"

"I really didn't expect that we would still have to go to the provincial capital!"

"......"

I heard these words from the mouths of two old farmers at the table opposite me. I glanced at them. Wrinkles covered their foreheads. Although their legs were still a bit strong, the reward for their hard work was telling them: they were already old. Such old people also have to go to the provincial capital. Are they going there to die? My heart was beating. Beating.

It was very quiet all around. Most of the shops were closed. Even those that were usually open on ordinary days, such as mountain goods stores, were also closed. After asking the waiter in the teahouse, I learned that because business was slow, they now only open during the bustling season, because the waiters have to find food elsewhere. Those who usually open their doors to do business now only do so during the bustling season. Speaking of the bustling season, it is also much deserted. In previous years, four or five dedicated ferries carried passengers, but this year there were not even half as many.

"It's getting worse every year."

In the final analysis, it's all the same sound. We also believe that no matter what place will be an "exception." When the time came, we left. As we boarded the ferry, we looked back at the lush countryside disappearing in the twilight.

Jiang Ruting Zhu Jiesheng Fallen Gold Fan

Zhonghua (1140) 9:00 PM to 9:45 PM

Opening chapter "Wu Shisi Part (2) Farewell Brother"

Wu the leader was sent on official errands. He was accompanied by his colleagues from the money exchange on his round trip. Wu Er went home to bid farewell to his brother and sister-in-law. Wu Dalang instructed him with tears streaming down. Brother, today I will part with you, I don't know when you will return home. Wu Er spoke with both feet firmly planted, saying, heroes also shed tears. Calling out to his brother, he said, don't worry. He turned his angry eyes to look at the charming woman. Sister-in-law, your junior has something to tell you, don't look down on my brother. If there are any mishaps, I will make sure your life is hard to keep. Jinlian heard and replied, saying that Wu Song's words were unreasonable. Your sister-in-law is not a man who wears a scarf and turban, but a boisterous female leader. Who dares to bully my dear brother, tell me quickly what the reason is. Dalang came to persuade from the side, saying, brother, you and I have a great relationship with each other. Your foolish brother will offer you three cups of wine today, to protect your body and relieve my worries. With emotions of both nature and nurture, tears flowed down. The colleagues urged Wu the leader. He lifted himself to bid farewell to his brother and sister-in-law, turning his head several times as he was leaving. Reluctant to leave his brother behind.

Yao Xiaoan Wang Pingqiu Qilin Leopard

Zhongxi (1040) 11:00 PM to 12:00 AM

Opening Chapter "Welcoming Spring"

The east wind has returned spring to the earth. All things are renewed and the atmosphere is restored. Go quickly to the eastern suburbs to welcome it. The flourishing ninety days have come again. Happily watching the plum trees in full bloom, auspicious symbols are tailored everywhere on the doors. Strike the spring ox. Brew new wine. Relatives and friends come for the New Year. Only feel that the scenery can make everyone happy, galloping and whipping, singing and dancing on the stage. Noble sons do not visit flower matters, planting thousands of red and purple brocades. The spring breeze points to the passing of time, the people happily return. The shadows of the trees sway, and the unlimited spring should be appreciated. The empty mountains and warm valleys have a harmonious atmosphere, only to see that the overlapping greens and layers of disease are not stained with dust. If one year meets the Spring Festival season, life will be difficult to extinguish. No need to trek to the ends of the earth, with heaven and earth as a garden and mountains and rivers to accompany. The world is gentle and full of fun, and there is nothing to do to unfold both eyebrows. Follow the curved waters and go to the mountain peaks, lingering in the middle stream for a few rounds. The water flows continuously along the stream, and the green mountains are folded back again. The scene of the three springs is unchanged every year, and the lively opportunity is taken by the plum blossom. Orioles leave the valley, and swallows linger. Several times the wind blows away the dust. The singing of birds and the fragrance of flowers are called beautiful things, how many times in life can one follow. Good times and beautiful shadows are difficult to describe, and the ladies praise them in unison. The flowers bloom slowly on the paths, and enjoy the leisurely return. Enjoy it as much as you can.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

Male and Female Actors Whose Luck Began After Fifty (Part 1) 239

— Ti Yun

A hundred kinds of businesses have been hit by the economic downturn, and the theater world is certainly not immune. But you haven't heard the actors themselves groaning and complaining. If you walk through the area around Broadway's Palace Theater, you will feel a desolate and bleak atmosphere. You will also feel how dark it is inside many theaters. You can't help but worry about the general actors.

You may not be too concerned about young actors. The women can become models, and the men can sell soda. But what about those old actors? How do they weather this storm? Maybe they have savings in the bank. Or maybe they have property in the countryside. But listen to a story about Fields (W. C. Fields).

Fields turned fifty. He thought he could retire and return to his hometown. He was also determined to retire. He had 250,000 in the Halibut Bank, enough to live a leisurely life. But Halibut Bank went bankrupt in the midst of the recession. You read that news in the paper. Many people in Hollywood were hit hard. And Fields was one of them. His fortune was gone. He not only couldn't retire, but had to start all over again. This is the most tragic thing. How can a person live another fifty years to enjoy leisure? But what can you say when things get to the critical point? As a result, he buried himself in hard work again.

He made many efforts to seek work in various large companies, but the general producers did not lower themselves to welcome him. Later, he had to lower his standards and perform in Mark Sennett's slapstick shorts. A glimmer of light gradually emerged on the dark horizon, but misfortune did not come singly, and he encountered another unexpected event. Everyone took him to the hospital, where he was seriously injured. His neck was broken. The doctors clamped his head up and put his neck in a plaster cast. They took down the calendar on the wall, fearing that he would be anxious if he looked at it.

He lay down for several months, more often unable to sleep, and he couldn't remember what year or month it was. It may have been God's cunning, deliberately tormenting him with illness, but after the illness, his fate took a turn for the better. Before he had fully recovered, Paramount had already sent someone with a contract, waiting at the hospital door. It turned out that his humor in the slapstick shorts had, through his misfortune, promoted everyone's attention.

Now Fields tells people: "I used to think it was a mistake to retire at fifty. The bankruptcy of the bank was a punishment for my laziness. Later, when I was saddened by the loss of money, fate broke my neck again. I now solemnly inform fate that I am no longer saddened by the bankruptcy of the bank, nor do I regret breaking my neck. Please, god of fate, do not give me pain and punish me again."

May Robson is also a female star who became famous in her later years. She is now stealing the limelight from the general glamorous young girls. She once came to New York because New York had added a great-granddaughter, and someone asked her. She replied: "Tired? I don't feel it at all. I'm going back to shoot a new movie right away. I'm only driving in second gear now. That's what Marie Dressler liked to say. She often said that she wanted to die on the job. She did die on the job. No one can understand the pain she suffered, but she was not a person who deserted the battle. That kind of spirit is also my spirit. I am fortunate to have that spirit as well. I am very busy in Hollywood. One movie hasn't finished filming, and another movie has started. They are demanding older women. I just happen to be an older woman, isn't that my luck?" (To be continued)

Film Review

Review of "Nell Gwyn" 240

— Ling He

Nell Gwyn - Greater Shanghai

"Nell Gwyn," starring Anna Neagle, is worth noting, at least in terms of the evaluation of film art. Under the excellent direction of Herbert Wilcox, her performance and the entire production technique have very good artistic achievements.

We have seen many films about palace history. Apart from the correct explanation of the producer's business plan, almost none of them have any other significance. Of course, some of them also depict the political secrets of a certain era, and even reflect the sufferings of the people. In this way, the audience has the opportunity to relive history and further explore science, which is by no means meaningless. Unfortunately, there are too few such films. What British and American producers are very interested in is still the romance in the palace. In the magnificent scenes and the glittering costumes, they use modern and sophisticated film techniques to confuse people in a paradise-like illusion, and then they smile triumphantly. In particular, this palace film, apart from seeing the romance between King Charles II of England and the actress Nell Gwyn, almost nothing more important historical events can be seen.

In this film, Charles II (played by Cedric Hardwicke) is written as a romantic emperor. He favors actresses, but he does not let actresses manipulate the government. He is an enlightened emperor, but also an affectionate man. Until his death, he still thinks of the actress, which gives people a deeply sympathetic impression. When we see the actress walking out of the palace alone in the early morning, we will not forget the desolate death of Charles II.

Here, we can clearly see that the playwright's technique of expression is indeed very well grasped. He simply grasps a few things to write, and explains all unnecessary processes with diaries or subtitles. He grasps the necessary points and writes them very fully. What we see is a very simple story, but it is concretely and figuratively expressed.

With a good script, it is of course much easier for the director. In addition to making the set very authentic and evoking a sense of nostalgia, he also pays special attention to the development of the play. Here we can put forward two points as examples for explanation. One is when the actress first enters the palace to see the king, she first reports the names of the dishes, etc., and very solemnly depicts the atmosphere of the court. At this time, the music is loud, setting off the haughty and arrogant demeanor of the Duchess (she is competing with the actress for favor) and the joyful laughter of the noble people. When the actress takes the stage, the music used for effect stops, causing the Duchess to suffer an embarrassing insult. The psychological description and even the air at the time are greatly enhanced with the help of sound. Secondly, what we want to put forward is the last scene, the air of death, the actress's crying, until the actress walks out of the palace alone, thanks to Monetgo's proper harmony and the domination of sound, the emotions at the time are indeed very well expressed.

As for the clarity of the personalities of the characters in the play, on the one hand, it is due to the excellent acting skills of the male and female protagonists, and on the other hand, we cannot deny the ingenuity of the director's technique. Apart from the insufficient content, this film is technically very beautiful.

Wesley Tunstall as the lawyer in "The Case" discussing matters with the female murderer in prison - Nanjing Screening

To Su Yin, Ling He, You Jing, Xin Zhi, Ti Yun, Wen Ying, Yuan Yi, Xiao Bai, Mao Di, Zheng Yan, Lin Ji, Zhen Ruo, Er Yin, Huang Yingdai, Zhou Hui, Hua, Dong Lin, Shu Min, Xue Mei, Bing Ru, Chang Xiong, Zha Dan, gentlemen: Thank you very much for your contributions to the January movie special issue. The accumulated expenses have now been settled. Please follow the following procedures for receiving remuneration and bring your slip to the accounting department of this museum within the specified dates to receive it!

Remuneration Procedures

The museum will issue remuneration from the 6th to the 10th of each month, and again from the 16th to the 20th, excluding Sundays, from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM at the accounting department of this museum. Please prepare a slip, affix the same seal as on the original manuscript, and proceed to collect the payment. If you are collecting for several months, you must provide slips and seals for each month separately for attachment to the ledger. As for the seal, regardless of the length of the article or the number of submissions per month, please affix a seal to each article for verification of the seal impression when collecting remuneration. Failure to affix a seal will be considered a waiver of remuneration. Furthermore, remuneration will be valid for six months from the date of publication. If it is still unclaimed by then, it will be considered that you do not wish to receive the remuneration, and the account will be cancelled for settlement purposes. The Movie Editorial Department of Shenbao.

Movie Novel

Voice of the Nation (Bordertown) (Part 1) 244

— Xue Mei

Produced by Warner Brothers of America, starring Paul Muni and Bette Davis

The face beneath the old, worn hat was serious, yet young, with piercing eyes and thin lips, characteristic of their race. His shoes were covered in the dust of a long journey. A truck approached him and slowly stopped. The driver grumbled, "Come on, jump in." The man standing on the ground asked, "Thank you... where are you going?" The driver said, "Straight south, a long way." "Alright, I'm going south too." He said, climbing up and sitting next to the driver. The truck then sped off with hundreds of horsepower.

That was Johnny Ramirez, born in Sonora Town, in the Mexican quarter of Los Angeles, the day he left his hometown to conquer the world. Johnny Ramirez—determined to work hard in this new world of gold, to become a second Lincoln, and to buy a Persian lamb coat for his mother. Johnny Ramirez—diligently studied law for several years at night school, and his name was mentioned in his graduation speech. Johnny Ramirez—his mother pawned her wedding ring to make him a sign, which read: "Johnny Farraday Ramirez, Attorney at Law."

The Ramirez family lived above a grocery store, with the sign hanging above the door. Anyone walking past this dirty street in the Mexican quarter, with pots and jars displayed on the side of the road, with frivolous youths wearing brightly colored clothes and darting eyes, with Mexican farmers wearing overalls, and the sounds of music and Spanish accents—anyone walking there would definitely see Ramirez's law firm sign. That was the only hope of his mother and the local teacher, to win some respect for them. The sign hung there for some time, but then it disappeared.

To put it simply, this is what happened. According to principle, Johnny Ramirez's case in the Mexican quarter was foolproof. A girl, still dressed in her half-night attire with makeup on her face, beautifully dressed, came to this dirty area with a boyfriend to appreciate the exotic scenery of this ethnic enclave. His powerful car suddenly spun around in the middle of the road and happened to crash into an old farmer's vegetable truck, smashing it to pieces and scattering the vegetables all over the ground. That old truck was the livelihood of the farmer's family. How could he now transport his goods between the town and the countryside? He stood there dumbfounded, tears streaming down his face. He was holding a card in his hand. The girl's boyfriend even told her not to give him the card. Fortunately, the girl had some conscience and gave him the card.

The next day, everyone was in court. The girl looked calm and fashionable. Her boyfriend was also in court; he was a famous lawyer. The vegetable farmer looked defeated and humble. His only hope was Johnny Ramirez. Johnny was also in court. He was wearing a shiny blue serge suit and stood before the judge, his black hair disheveled. He gestured frequently with his arms as he spoke. Because of the anger in his heart, he could not help but sweat profusely.

But in the Plaza Chapel, Ramirez's mother knelt before the statue of the Virgin, praying: "Merciful Virgin, grant that my son may win this case, just this once. I have prayed repeatedly, just this once—or he will be heartbroken. Merciful Mary... help him... I don't want a fur coat... I only ask to win this case..." (To be continued)
